Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it in the old days "contused cure", and you will do to the patient who has this disease that hairs will have or front, then he makes III cuts on the front evenly according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the incisions be as II should go all through the forehead down to the ear, and the other II as II ribs above the cheekbones, and keep yourself from the incision of the arteries that are at the II ribs above the cheekbones; and remove your hand from the continuation of the II jawbones, and let each wound be the quantity of III does across; and have prepared a piece of sponge and much of cloth for wiping the blood, then put the spatula sharp of II parts of this which is the form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision which is below the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the kernel that is between the two incisions to the entire surface that is on the bone, then make another part from the middle incision to the other second one, and then extract far this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If it is put into the first fissure the instrument which is called "cultellaire", and is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the rib cutting toward the flesh toward the heart, and the rib itself toward the bone, and the point until it reaches the middle fissure. 
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head as eyes until the incision is continuous to those that open the heart, and then another part make in the middle fissure until the other end; and then extract the blood equally, and express it out there for the blood taken; then put in each fissure a tent of old cotton, and put over cloths moistened in wine and oil and aisil, and keep that no abscesses come; and on the third day untie the ligature, and there administer great poultice of tepid water, then the cure of basil ointment with rose oil, and other cures of which one heals wounds, until it is healed.  
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When to any come catarrh acute customarily, and you see the eyes sunk in and small, and weakening of sight, and the papers burned; and the hair falls out, and where chief in they do a pain acute, and the sick one sneezes; therefore know by these accidents that those matters and this catarrh ne comes from many veins, and the change cure that is, so is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to raise his forehead, then make a great fissure in the middle of the forehead, and another through the wide I-beam.  
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begins from the fissure of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move to eat; and when the bone is uncovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then sew between the two lips of the fissure and put old cotton there, and linen bandages; then tie above with cloths moistened in wine and oil, and guard against a hot abscess; when it is removed, it is necessary that you rub the bone until cartilage begins to grow, then treat it with drying things that cause cartilage to form. 
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In such manner: take .ij. parts of flower of wheat, and .iiij. parts of colofine, and make thereof a plaster; and administer it in these wounds to cause flesh to grow throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of four things: or grains, or beast, or stone or semblance such as iron; or seed, such as peas, beans, lentils; or flowing thing such as water and oil and semblance things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear, stone or any other thing that does not join to the ear, nor grows in the ear, put the ear in the sun. 
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see a stone, if there distills any drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and have him sneeze from condiments, and stop his nostrils when the sneezes come, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and keep the ear upwards. 
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times a fever comes from this cure; and if it does not come fever, to him administer the extraction as pincers subtle, of which here is the form. 
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with the tweezers, that is good; if not, administer extraction with a fine, double-edged needle; and if it does not come out by this, make a cane of iron and thrust the head of the cane or puncture of the ear strongly, and stop those around the cane with soft wax so that no air can enter there with the cane; then try to pull it out, for many times it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, take a piece of glue that is used to catch birds, and put it on any instrument that is pointed for this purpose, and put a dab of cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and try to pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not come out of all these things that we have said, then you must hurry to cut the ear thus as an abscess comes and spasms; and the manner of cutting it is that you first bleed the patient from the cephalic vein, and extract blood according to the measure of his virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear to the fat or where it depends; and let the cut be like a crescent moon, as far as you come to the bone, then the bone according to your strength, and suck it diligently with your mouth; and the cure until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grains that are inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer one spatula thin according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision to that grain.  
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think that the grain is moist because of the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract with fine tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction be gentle.  
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the ear then that falls down it is necessary for the patient to use a remedy of first condition and fill the ear with old cotton.  
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie on that same ear where the water is. 
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out for this, it is good. 
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not so, take many stones according to the length of your thumb, light and fine, and heat them a little in the fire; and put one on the patient's ear where it hurts, and raise it up from his feet with another foot, and set another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this from stone to stone until the water flows entirely, and thus it will all flow out; and if you see it, take a reed, and put one end in the ear, and the other end put into fire until the most tender reed burns; then do another part of reeds until the water flows completely, as we have said about the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small body, such as a flea and similar thing, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of great body that one can feel it, then administer the extraction with forceps; and this is the lightest thing to remove which is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you cure them as we have said in the division and where we treat distillations, and the cure does not help, then it behooves you to look at the ear in the sun: if there appears no worms, then you treat them with subtle forceps, and if they do not appear, then take the instrument of which this is the shape:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow below and wide above.  
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And put the most subtle chief into the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then succeed and form to all the chain; make this often as long as all the worms come out. 
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey to this, stuff the ear with cotton as I said in the case of stones; and if they do not protrude far as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the excision of worms, and you will find them treating distillations; and distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all these instruments, for this is the form as you see:  
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be of silver or brass, narrow below to one little holes, and wide above to distill; and for pressing within the distillation one instrument of brass well made for this, and if you see take one razor and wrap around the point conveniently cotton; then I throw your oil or your juice, and what you want from your medicines into the canine, and the canine be in the ear; then put within the razor to all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or at the end of the ear; and feel the patient inside, and let the distillations one pock be warmed by the fire then one distills it into the ear; and keep that it be not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without any holes in their ears; and this same thing happens to men by clogging of a wound, or of flesh born inside the ear, and these blockages come sometimes from deep within the ear, if one cannot see them; and sometimes they happen i.e. one point of fire, and it can be seen well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes from deep within if one cannot see it, is of great damage in many dispositions, and in this, you should put the ear of the sick person to the sun; and look inside: if you see the apparent opening, then the work has all this spatula form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be sharp and trenchant in front and behind all plain, so that it does not bleach the ear; if the opening is of flesh born or a part of the ear, then hold it with subtle pincers, and cut lightly, until that flesh is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the suppuration is in the ear, take a thin razor light and heat it a little at the fire, then put it in the body of the ear. 
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the opilation of which the patient feels great pain in hearing, pierce lightly, and keep that you do not wound the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a tent according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment. 
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this with no day until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and powder on powdered vitriol; and if you see the ear swollen, then it is necessary that you pull out the tent and move another tent moistened in cerote which is made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding comes, then dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other cures that stop the bleeding which are or treated by distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the skin of the papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This althlul that comes in papers of the eyes when they are moist and are dry, then it is necessary that you extend them with tweezers and pincers, and the cut off with a spatula from its roots; then put on their place powdered vitriol.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without it decorts, then cauterize them with the subtle lentil cautery, and the cauterization after incision is worth a move; and many times they return, because nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return at all.
de la gresle	of the groin
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come in the papers of the eyes things that seem glassy in their shape and in their hardness, and for this reason this illness is called “hailstorm,” and it is an assembly of moisture thick in the paper above and below; the work is such: take warde if the hailstone moves from one part and another, and this is a light thing to know; then do it with the broad edge, then the scab of each part lightly, then take it with the tweezers, and the cut. 
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it without feeling a bit of the paper, do not harm the patient; and if the tear is large, assemble it with a suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not use force, for the flesh will restore itself soon and cause no scarring.  
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the gravel is descending into the inside of the ear toward the top part, then turn over the paper, and being the gravel with tweezers, and cut it and press on one side and the other; and if the paper is separated by the incision, it grieves nothing; and when the gravel is cut, let leave the eye of salty water, and cure the place from that which prevents flesh as long as the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	This is a fatty substance which is produced in the membranes of the eyes above and this happens more to children than adults, and it grieves much their eyes, and they come down with catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears hasten to their eyes; and for that reason they lie down on their faces sideways, and sleep on top, and are their membranes under their eyebrows moist so that the swelling and appearance have covered with exinach which opens in the eye.  
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place with your thumbs and feel the exit between them. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of working it is that the patient puts his head on your thigh; and then take one drapeil of linen, and prepare a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains exinach from each part, then place it on top; and press with your fingers on one side and the other so that the exinach is assembled within the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture with a spatula trenching a fissure of the width, and not be more than large as the wound made on the vein's opening; and making the skin in parts until you reach the exinach; and in many dispositions comes exinach from the fissure, according to the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract then with a whole piece of cloth between your fingers on the outside, and turn your hand to right and left until it is spread; and keep that you do not add in the fissure, that you do not reach all the spatula up to the eye, that you do not blind it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exit does not open at the beginning of the split, so gently widen the split until it opens; then extract as we have said, then moisten bandages in oil and water, and put them on top, and restrain with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if to such men who grind seeds and put on top to corrupt the moisture which is delayed.  
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal until it is healthy.  
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the place of a hot abscess, so treat with plasters soothing until it is healed.  
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When on papers hairs are born aligned other than the natural, and are grown, they harm the eyes, and bring manners of maladies as tears accustomed and softening of the papers and albuginea, until it is cause of the destruction of the eyes; and is the cure according to .iiij. manners: or by cautery entire fire, or by medicine ague according to what it is before or chapter of cautery, and is done or by incision and stitching or by canes, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It behooves you to put the head of the patient in your healthy one, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, it puts an needle to all .i. thread above; and let it be below the margin of the paper or where the hair grows near these hairs, and draw .i. thread to the top of the paper, and turn it to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the aligned hairs, to all the spatula, from the great tear to the small; then extract .i. thread, and put under the paper a small tent of cotton and cloth, then lay on the paper a figure of enche, like the leaf of myrtle, and nevertheless it behooves that the figure be according to the quantity that you see to raise the paper which is divided to all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is one who needs it, cut a large quantity of the paper according to how softened the paper is; then make a whole spatula on the two lines that you have marked, and start with wide tears up to small ones; and let one of the slits be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the scalpel into one of the two angles of the heart, then peel it completely; then assemble the two lips with a suture of a needle with all the fine wool thread, and wipe away the blood, and make air to flow on the excess of hair above the two eyebrows with nothing sticky, if you want to do this; and if not, take care of it, then leave the suture and the hairs up to three days or four; then treat the wound without sutures with dry and constricting things, because the paper comes back together with the joining of the wound and its assembly, but the suture is moving (as the ancients say), and this work without fear; and in another manner: and it is that you mark the paper with a figure which is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have counted, at three scalpel points according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut what rises above the small strengths equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you do not have the power to hold the pliers, and the thing is not equal, take a needle which has thread, and put it in the middle of the figure; and put the other thread along the great tear, and the second thread along the small one, and assemble between your two threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin over what you have signed, as we have counted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by stitching, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointment; and sometimes it happens that the hair of the paper are converted: so it is necessary that you use what we have said about the incision; but the suture in one and the other is more artificial.  
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the cauteries is as follows: and it is that you convert the paper and its make inside according to what I have said, and then make two cauteries by art, and two threads subtle also long as the paper and the width of the spatula is; and cut the two heads from two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble the one and the other subtly upon those that summit over the paper of the eye, and strain the two cauteries of the two parts form; and let it thus for some days, and the skin which is strained will die and shrink and hold, as long as it seeks by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed, if the wound has strength, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is joined together, and if the paper is lifted, and they will no longer prick the hairs; and this is the form of the two cauteries that you shall make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide: 
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a fine needle, and it puts 1 silk thread fine and subtle; then assemble the shoulders and knot them one and the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then order in the chase another fine silken thread briefly, and knot the chief of the two threads; then put the patient's head on your healthy; and let it be towards the sun so that the work is clear, because it is a subtle and small work, then put the needle to all the chase into the root of the hair adjusted, and make it pierce the paper hastily until you draw it above the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the chase, and put in the chase that hair, if there are 1 or 2 or 3 or more; then extract your hand until the hairs come out all the chase in the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, so you will draw the chase down to all the thread that you have ordered it, until the chase comes out from the hole above and you see it by the vision of the eye; then you will draw the chase and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for 2 or 3 days, until the hair hardens in its place and lets the flesh grow up; and if the hairs are small, accompany 1 long hair from the natural ones, and let it be raised with that one or you leave it, until it is lengthened and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the rot of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this sickness which is called "aleacrati" or the rot comes to the eye, there are two ways: one natural and the other unnatural.  
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by sudden blow of a wound, or cutting or cautery, and similar things. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of the work in it is that you split that suture, and separate the lips of it, and put inside tents of linen, and leave it until it is healed; and it is not right that you use in the cure of it things that dry and constrict. 
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the sickness returns worse than at first; but there is a work of softening things, such as fennel; and rose water or alcohol and flaxseed cooked, and oil of diaquillon melted in any oil, and wrapped in a tent, and cure it with this.  
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not close according to the form it was before; and this work that we have said is nothing but a treatment for this illness, that it may not return according to the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh which comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is dislocation is truly called “axacrati”, and it is natural and accidental. 
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidents come from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the way of the work is that you prick a needle, which has a double thread, and stick it in the flesh, and make it go from the left tear to the right, so that the thread comes into the two cheeks of the flesh; then hold the flesh above the entire needle, and cut with a spatula wide.  
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what is fitting, it is good; if those are not, then take the razor and put it in the fissure, and turn the paper, and make II fissures where cost it inside the paper; and be the heads of the II fissures of the II angles of the incision that you have cut, and be made an angle so that when they are assembled, that the figure is as the figure of a letter which has no «I griesche»; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its costs are raised from below, of what follows the paper, then adjust the II parts severed, and the cout of a thread of wool; then cure of those that we have said of mollifying medicines, and of tents, as long as it is healed. 
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a rupture or stitch or cautery, it is necessary that you make a plain cut under the hairs of the papers, and according to what is said above; then bind between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the illness, because it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters equip everything of all their power how it makes return the figure to its natural form; and the sick man himself, according to what is necessary of work and instruments in many dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture occurs to hands of men in such a manner that the paper above is sewn with the white of the egg, and cannot move nor make its natural works, then it is necessary that you put the point of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and the while as pinches, until you cut what is attached to the spatula, subtle, which is not too sharp nor too blunt, so that the patient may not suffer that the spatula be too sharp nor pierce the eye; and let your incision, with which you scrape together that assembly, be slight, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and it is healed all that assembly, and do at no time in the eye salt water, and the lift of sweet water, and of collier; then put between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and put on top of the eye wool moistened in abundance of egg; and after the third day use the collier and things soothing until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the angle of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the angle is in .ii. manners: it is nervous and seeming to .i. hard syfac, and another which is not nervous but is seeming to white moisture congealed, that when one touches it with iron and one cuide panre as pinces, it cannot om; and the one and the other semblance commences towards the great tear, and crosses poc and poc until it covers all sight and all light and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of the incision is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then the one opens the eyes; and lifts the paper with your hand, then coil the angle as pinces with a small doubleure, and the one on top; then take a needle, and put in it .i. hair of horse, or calf, or ox, and .i. strong thread; and double the point of the needle a poc and place it into the angle, and pierce it through the whole needle, and tie the angle with a thread and the one on top, and scrape at all the hair the side of the angle which follows the prunele and silk to the hair until the head, then cut the remaining in the root of the tear to all the spatumile subtle and as small forces, and leave the flesh naturally or tear, so that by the incision does not come the body of tears customarily; and no times is the angle on the one only, and to the thread, as we have said; then the scraping one has all the spatumile souef of this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and tear it, and that the needle is not pierced; and after the incision put in the eye a little bit of ground silk, and from the collar made of lead ore, and leave it until the next day; then cure it as it is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerved, and you cannot push the needle, and the tweezers cannot enter, many times this semblance of a nail is cured with medicines; and they grow as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it covered, so operate on the eye of the patient, and take the spatula light point acute according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the nail up subtly, and if you see that it diminishes not and the reason hastens, then distill from your mouth into the eye collar made of lead ore and red collar and ground silk, and plug the eye until the next day; then begin the other work according to this same operation, as long as it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If no thing is contrary to you in the eye, such as an abscess of chaus, then milk it, and cure first the abscess hot until it be healed, then begin again the work as before, until it be healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh by the tear hurts in the eye by great annoyance, then suspend it to the bone and in cut a part and not half too, that body of tears doesn't come; then distill in the eye colic red which is made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that arises on the iris
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	The eyes of some men are born sometimes red and cover the eyelid and restrain upon the papers and turn to the fire, and seems like a rose of the balcony; and the work is that the patient puts his head in your healthy, then he opens the eyes, and coil all that flesh with suitable needles to those, and holds it with force; then cuts the first flesh, and goes cutting to the razor until the end, and keep that you do not bleed the eye during the operation; and let the incision be of the spatula as we have said in the incision of the angle and the small forces of which one removes the shell, as the form after this chapter shows it; and when the incision is completed and all the flesh is removed, then apply the oil of silk crushed or you distill red ochre and similar corrosive medicines, and put upon the eye fire cotton with yolk of egg, so that it be assured of hot pus; and if it remains nothing, and the blood of your body is mounting, and you doubt hot pus, so leave the eye and cure the pus with things soothing the hot pus; then return to your work as long as it is healed, and so do until all the flesh is attached in the eye by this resemblance. 
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless it is necessary that you apply the cure of each weak oil from the natural way; and from the accidental way, in the work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works as long as you see that this member be undergoing that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Red veins are seen that are covered over the eye, and they take away from the sight its function and weaken the eye every day. 
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is therefore necessary for the first that you look if the eye, in what it is, is affected, and there is no other disease except the cataract; therefore, command the patient to put his head on your shoulder, then support those veins all around according to his knowledge, and let the incisions be subtle double according to this form:  
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let the two outlines by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then the coil as forces those veins subtly, and wipe the blood hour after another, until you see remove those veins out of the eye; and guard that you do not prick the eye with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at the hour of midday before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cut further than those veins; and when you will have done this, then distill in the eye green and red collyrium to corrode what is remained of the red vein.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect all of these in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye of things soothing the pain of the eyes, and let it for some days until the pains are calmed and it is assured of a hot abscess, then begin again according to this manner which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of forces.
de la fistule de l’oil	of the eye fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire is called "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and with medicine burning according to those that I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is something in it that you cut into the abscess, where it must die, and treat all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you will see the corruption and the blackness, if the king has all the instruments of what here is the form; and it is called «aspre chief», and it is made of iron one head, and it is pointed like a file as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little while you know that this corruption is reset; and do this several times, then restore the place with medicinal drying agents.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the leus is soldered, and flesh grows there, and the body of the bow is soldered, and remains so for XL days, and it does not renew and is not in any way an abscess, know that it is healthy; if this is not the case, if there is no other remedy than to bring the fistula back to the opening according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time by iron, and by sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered, take the forest according to this form, and let the shoulder be of iron at III angles, and the shaft be thinned up to the head as you see here: 
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone below the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then turn to all sides until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through what comes in this, if he holds his hand on his cheek; and then return to the place of dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the joints, then the matter goes to the cheek; so it is a lighter thing for the patient. 
de l’issue de l’oil	of the issue of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are open and throughout entirely, and nothing comes to disturb the forehead, nor diminishes, then it is necessary that you bind the patient; then heal, then place suction cups or a halter without hurting for sucking, then put on the eye  1 layer made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolla, and then strain the eye, and plaster above with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths soft enough, and double each one in 4, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye has need for; then strap it from above with a strong bandage, and restart the suction cups for sucking without hurting; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the layers soften, it is necessary that you tighten it very much; then remove the layer after the day and night, and if you see the eye healing, it is good; if not; then restart the plaster and cloths and the layer and suction cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the dislocaiton of a sleeve
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruption comes in the sleeve, then open it, and it comes out like a piece of resin, grain by grain, and is easy to see; therefore if you see it covered, the work is such that you put a needle at the root of the lower part until the upper one, then put another needle where there is one double thread from the lachrymal part; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the disposition; then cut the place of the double thread and tie one part of the vine around, and restrain it well, then extract the needle and put over the other eye half in a circle of an egg; and let him until the threads fall with the vine, then cure the eye with comforting things as long as the wound is healed; and any time the wound is restrained by the vine on each side by a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes show a great appearance, then pierce them with a fine spatula that comes from the eye itself, and correct the albuminous moisture and descend the eyes, and enter into them immediately; then extract it as long as it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the eye cavity
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This sickness which is called «alcunnati» is nothing else than a bow which is assembled in the eye, seeming like water descending, and it is not water; and the manner of the appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit on the prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands of two parts, and move it as much as you see the bow come upward to your eyes; then be sure, and do not descend and let it be disordered the light, and let the patient see things as if he would; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descending of the bow is not prepared as we have said.  
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the sharp spatula and go upon the cornea with a prick along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the corona, until the bow is issued; and when it is issued, distill in the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek boiled and honey, then be cured with another cure until it is healed. 
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye's sharp points
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the likeness of swords in the division, and those that it befits to examine; so work according to healthiness.  
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands crossed, away from the sun's light, and bind his healthy eye and hold it firmly; then place the paper of the eye on your left hand if the eyes are left, or on your right hand if the eyes are right; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are left, the instrument which is called “almagda,” or with your left hand, if the eyes are right; then put the point of the instrument beside the crown by the thickness of a fingernail in that whiteness of the eye at the part of the tear duct's lower end, then push the instrument called "almagda" carefully, and straighten your hand until it pierces into the white of the eye, and feel that the almagda comes to the empty space; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda be at the full extent of the space that is from the pupil to the end of the darkness; and this is the crown of the eye; so you will see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the corneal web, and then put the instrument up to where the liquid is, then express it out of one way after another.  
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water descends now, the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye. 
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After rest a little, and if the water returns by the second way, put the force with the instrument, and when it is ens fixed and it does not rise, extract the algida lightly by turning your hand back and forth; and then put back in water a bit of seil gemme, and leave out of this the oil inside. 
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by means of a cloth, or moistened rag in oil rose and in abundance of egg, and tie with the healthy eye. 
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on top a mixture of ground up with an abundance of egg. 
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter into the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have their eyes too hard, then it is necessary that you prick the instrument which is called "alberit," of this it is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce therefore the conjunctive alone, and do not go too deeply in by force, but make it subtle, then put almagda as we have said; and at the completion of the work equip the patient with the bed beforehand, in which he sleeps on his back in the dark place; and be devoid of all movements, and eat light meats, and do not move your head neither to the right nor to the left, and be bound according to his disposition up to the third day; then untie it in the same dark house, and try his sight, and let him see some things, and then put the ligature back until the seventh day; and it does not come that you do this in the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you align this, for those who rise quickly. 
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When an abscess comes, that you should unbind the eye before the seventh day, and apply a poultice to those who soothe the abscess; and when it is appeased, then unbind the eye and put upon its face a small piece of cloth to cover any day, and let it be in that dark place. 
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then it goes out of the house to and fro, and converts itself into its cases; and know that none of the disciples must interfere in this case. 
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in their country they made almond pierce, to which one sucks the liquid, but nonetheless I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the resemblances of the forms of almonds, for those who do not know them see them; and they are properly of arrain.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let the head of these be of the same subtlety, and the last in three angles acute.
de la char sor le neis	of the bone about the birth
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	At times, diverse conjoined joints are born, of which some seem like scorpions with many feet; and if there are such ones where the flesh is discolored from wood, and if it has flesh of good color. 
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of these wounds which are raw and not yet crusted, it is necessary for you to make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open his nostrils, and place the oncin on those wounds, and pull them out; then cut what you can hold with the fine sharp spatula on one side, until you know that this wound is completely cleaned. 
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any thing remains that one cannot cover, open it completely, i.e., with subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if without the swarm or abscess clothes, secure it as it is proper; and if it is malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize it until the blood is extinguished and all the pus is removed, then pour in water or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose works and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is cartilage in the bone above, which prevents the instruments from coming to cut: therefore it is necessary that you put I thread of linen a bit thick, and be knotted by hand, and have between each knot a space of little or less; and put the patient's shoulder on the thread in his nose at the tip, and pull by smelling until it comes out through the nose inside the mouth; and many times do children so in schools, and it is a light thing to him who wants to do it; then hold the head which comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head which comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and feel each one after the other, being careful as to where the threads are. 
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do what you know that the new have corrupted that flesh, then treat the wound, wipe the blood, and moisten the wound in Egyptian ointment, and put it back straight to the nose as before; do this III days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that is left of flesh; and then put on the nose a band of wool for some days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the nose, to which one distills the oils and medicines in the nose. 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And be it of silver or iron, resembling an open lamp, as a basin, and lead it thusly; and if you see fit, make a closed basin, and have the instruments clean for purging the head; and let it have one handle on the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquor.
de la char sor le neis	of the bone about the birth
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.
