Many times at the head of the bone a malady which is called "telul" is born, and grows and becomes great onwards, until it is visible to behold; and for this you should cut it at the beginning, and pull all out the bone, then put on its place the cautery or the burning medicine; and if one delays to cut it until it is great, then take care if it is hard, of foul color, of poor feeling: if not touch it with iron because it is an infected abscess, for when one cuts it any time, it comes great misfortune to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touching, not of foul color, and you see that one can cut it all, then empty the patient and cut it without fear, and cure the place with drying and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the bone is cut and closed
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuation comes in one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, because in no men. 
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary that when this happens to anyone, if you see that the wound is fresh and full of blood; and then join the two lips together with a suture, and treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already opened on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scar all parts of their center until they heal, then bring the two lips together with a suture, and restrain them, and powder on top of dragon's blood powder, and ground incense; and put on top of the powders a piece of strong ointment or another binding ointment, and leave it until it dries out by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed. 
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the suture is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the suturing of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In men's mouths there happen abscesses hard, resembling grains of sand, and smaller and larger; therefore it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cleave on each knot, and take with pincers and cut in each part; then apply to the place after incision of ground vitriol, until the blood be stanched; and then the ointment of oil, and cure the place with dry things until it be healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times there is born on the gums flesh attached, which the ancients call "albulus"; therefore it is necessary that you hold it with pliers and cut it at its root, and leave to flow the pus or blood; then put on the place ground vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders; and if that flesh returns after the incision, and many times happens, so cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return after cauterization; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of deaf people
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs which are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellowish and green, as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth are foul-smelling; so you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his jaws be in your saint, and remove the teeth or scabs appearing, until nothing remains; and thus do with the blackness and greenish color, and yellowness and other spots, as long as they are visible; and if one removes those that are at the first reason, it is good; if those not, then it begins again to scrape the second day and the third, until you have removed everything; and know that teeth need different types of instruments to remove, according to what the work demonstrates to you, because the rasp used to remove outer teeth has other forms than that which removes between the teeth; and these forms and others be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you take care to drain as much as you can, because one must not do otherwise; because it is a very high substance until one has no excuse for scraping.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to drink, it behooves you to be certain of the tooth aching. 
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain afflicts the patient, and he thinks that it is a toothache, and makes milk from the good tooth; and nevertheless, the pain does not depart at all by this, as long as the evil remains, because we have already done this to our elders; and when you are well certain of the aching tooth, then it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth on all sides with a spatula. strong to protect the gums from all parts; then move it with your two fingers or tongs subtly at the first point and point, until it is well loosened, then hold firmly with the pliers; and let the head of the patient be in your lap between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.  
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After the tooth is extracted straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and put it gently inside each side, and move it like you did at first.  
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and broken, it behooves you to fill it with cloth, where the holes are; and hold it carefully with tweezers so that it does not break when held; and it behoove s most skillfully to work around the gum to loosen the tooth. 
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And so give good care that you do not break it, and remain a part of it, and return to the patient by the malice of the root greater pains than the first. 
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And guard that you do not do as the ignorant healers do, who by their haste and boldness sometimes break the bone, and do not bring them what we have recounted; but they cause to come many times by the opening of those great illnesses for the roots that remain there, or for the bone they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled, wash its place with wine or oil and salt; and if a bleeding comes, which often happens, apply the place of vitriol powder; and if that does not work, cauterize it. 
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, to which one must file teeth first, should be with long points and thick handles so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be thick members so that they do not bend when pulling, and be well-made iron, and be toothed for grip.
de la racine des dens	From the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in the breast, it is necessary that you put on top moistened cotton in butter one or two days. 
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	as long as the eyes are softened, then put in the tongs that are called “algefri”, so that the shoulder seems like a bird's beak; and be inside made as well as a file and this is the form: 
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tongs, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh around the root, and there put the instrument which is called "althali," that is to say a spatula, because of its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be it strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out by those means, it is good; if those do not, then help yourself with all the instruments, of which the forms come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument which has two prongs, of which shape comes here:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before in the direction of the teeth, and of this instrument which resembles a large pair of tongs, of which shape comes here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And be this instrument so that it may not break, and know that many instruments are of teeth; and also other instruments, which are not mentioned; and the wise masters subtle find by themselves their instrument, according to what their works and the disease show them, for there are such diseases where the ancients do not teach any instrument for the diversity of others and if one breaks not a bone or other bones, or where it can be broken, then search for the instruments that you need, which I have told you, and help yourself with gestures, according to what is here the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well holding to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but it can hold and remove; and then restore its place with medicines suitable for these, and if there is in the bone rot, and it is small, then the king has all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body, and the form is ugly, and especially in virgin women, then it is necessary that you know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and one cannot file or smooth it; therefore, the ray; and if it is with the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is here, and is similar to a small beak, and be of sharp iron at its summit:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cup is put and put in hands for several days for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be filed, then the file of a kind of file as this is its form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file that one makes needles with; and in filing the tooth little by little in several days lightly, so that it does not move until it falls; then the plane at the end has no trace, and if the tooth is too sharp and it pricks the tongue, then it is necessary to file the roughness until it is equal, so that it does not prick the tongue nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth is loosened, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on it so that it moves without falling out, and you have treated them with constricting medicines, and this does not work; if it is necessary to restrain it with a gold thread, because the silver thread becomes green and corrodes, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth are close together, then take the thread and put it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the loosened teeth between the sound teeth, if there is one or more, until you come cleverly to the sound tooth on the other side; then begin the covering again up to the place where you began, and strain your hand subtly and cleverly, so that it does not move; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. 
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then hold the jaw bones with pliers and assemble them, and put them between a sound tooth and put it so that it does not bite the tongue; and then leave it this way as tight as it can stay, and if it loosens, or the wires are broken, then restrain it with another wire; let it remain and serve in this way all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two bad ones, as you see. 
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls, then it is put back in its place, from fresh to fresh, as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not wise and experienced, and sometimes the form of a tooth of bone of the vein is made, and it is put in the place where the deficiency is, and it is restrained as we have said, and remains and serves like this for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	At no time is this ligament that comes from under the tongue or nature, that one is born thus; or by accident of a wound joined together; and the work is such that you operate on the mouth of the patient, and have his head in your hand, and lift the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament wide, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, and this is from the joining of a wound, then you put the awl in and cut wide that ligament; and keep that the incision be not too deep, for the artery which is below; and when you have done, lift the dew of rose water and of ease, or of cold water, then put under the tongue a tent of linen; and stitch the patient every night, that the place may not be joined. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, put on the place powdered vitriol; and if the blood does not stop, cauterize it with the dull cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed. 
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of rusty color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, then touch it not, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining to whiten, and there is moisture, then put in the probe, and make it with a fine spatula, and deliver it on one side and the other; and if the bleeding does not stop at your work, then put on powdered vitriol until it is bleached, then return to your work until you extract all pus; then lift the place with vinegar and salt, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Of abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes come from within the throat bumps that are called «godath», and they call them properly the II almonds, and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, if take care: if it is a hard abscess of small size and fusse color, do not touch it with iron.   
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also for the decorrement of blood; but let it alone until it is mature, and then you will split it, or it would break by itself; and if it is of white color again, and the root is subtle, have prepared the instrument to cover, but first look whether the abscess calms down and is appeased. 
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore make the patient sit before the sun, and his arms be in good health, and he works the mouth and the tongue of the pliers between his hands, and presses the tongue below to all the instrument, from this is the form; and be it of silver or iron subtle like a knife: 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And you press the tongue on all this instrument, and you see the abscess, so take the oncine and put it in the almond, and push it upwards more than you can; and do nothing of the cloths with, then the cope to the instrument, of this is the form, that seems ones forces; and nevertheless the chief are curved, and one place the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron inde or d’andainne:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, so you cope it with pliers, of this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be cutting on one side, and the other side no; and when you have cut one of the almonds, so cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient hot water, and water and thus, and if a discharge of blood happens, so gargle the patient with water, or peels of pomegranates that are cooked, or leaves of myrtle, and similar things, until the wound be cleansed; then cure it as long as it be healed; and at no time rise in the throat other abscesses than the two almonds, so cut them then just like the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman of an abscess that was inside her throat, that is to say the small abscess; and I had well almost closed all of the throat, so that the woman could not expire through the conduit which was stopped up, and could not eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained thus one day or two.  
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high it had to have been put in two reigns by the two openings of the nose. 
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I therefore did, and placed one in the one nostril, then pulled the other outside, and in the other a large portion of bowel; then I put another piece in the other nostril, and opened its mouth and pressed the tongue; after placing the instrument in these abscesses, and scooping out part, only a little blood came out; and so was unstopped the conduit of the throat of the woman, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut that abscess for long time; and the abscess grew back full, and filled the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; therefore I burned and cauterized it inside the throat: thus remained without growing; and I departed from these parts, and know only that God did with her after me. 
de l’uve	of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When it is rolled up to the vein, and it is filled and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is short and round, it is called "vein". 
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the head of the abscess is appeased, and it is subtle, then it behooves you to cut it; and the one which is rounded assembled and is not long; and it is sanguine or of fuschia color or black, then it behooves you to escape the incision of it. 
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great peril upon the patient.  
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and of its length, that you make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue to the instrument of which we have made mention before; then insert the awl into the eye, and remove it, and the coping to the one of the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds.  
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut more, it grieves the voice, and the speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the II almonds, and cure it until it is healed.  
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid to be cut, it is necessary that you use an implement to the cauterization of the senses fear. 
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp acute. 
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head on your healthy side, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we have said or in the chapter of cautery, and confides with a sharp quick cloth, so that it is not too thick nor too light; and in using the end of this instrument, for this reason here is the form: 
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it has or chief a hair where one puts the medicine, as like the handle of a spoon, and put the instrument to all the medicine on the grape; and the patient be lying on his side, so that the saliva and the muscle correct from his mouth of the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the palate; then hold your hand to all the medicine and press it on the grape, the quantity of half an hour, as long as you see it burning and the irritations of the medicine are appeased; and if you see it, take cotton and envelop it on any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument to all the cotton in the cavity above, until the cotton dries on the grape; and do this often, as long as the cauterization is perfect, then leave it dry, and lie after four or five. And if you have need to restart the cautery of the medicine, start it again, and after the cautery wipe around the grape, with cotton buttered, and purify what is around the medicine; and be rinsed with cold water, and be cured by gargles as long as it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, nor the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calament and ysope and origanum and rue and camomille and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in one pot, and put it therein, and make boil; and let the pot be well glued with strong earth, and inside the pot have one instrument hollowed according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And be it of silver or of iron, and let one of the heads [be] put in the mouth of the sick person until the vapor rises to the uvula by the vein, until the uvula is dead; after that, he begins again, until the uvula dries, and keep that you do not make this at the beginning of the coming of the hot abscess, for many things happen; and do not make this except at the declination of the hot abscess. 
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a dog and put inside its head a piece of lead, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the piece of lead does not make the vapor heavier in the mouth, and it is good treatment and whole salvation. 
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a thorn or fish spine gets lodged in the throat, or something else; so it behooves you to draw out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see move the thing. And what does not appear to you and is returned to the throat, it behooves you to make the sick person vomit thus as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps then the thing will be released by vomiting; or the sick person swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or one morsel of dry bread; and tie to the sponge one thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will lodge itself, and then draw it out further; and if it does not come out through what we have said, then take one instrument of wood according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it can more easily enter into the throat, and have the head lifted high; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest all come undone, nor put the bone inside; and it is better that the patient puts out the instrument, for he will know if the thing is blocked; so he pushes down, or he draws back the whole instrument equally until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	Of the bleeding of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes medicine is given to the sick without using medication; and when this does not help, then look at the throat of the sick person in the sun, then that you press his tongue with the instrument I told you about.  
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the snare, then treat it with all small tweezers, or subtle pliers that are suitable for this. 
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, then take a shaved dog and put it in the throat of the sick person, then put where the tail is, make it hot iron, and do this often. 
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And the patient stays in water all day.  
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full a cup of cold water, and work the mouth, and place it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the patient feels the water, he will fall.  
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, for it will cure without fail. 
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot or it has burning charcoal, and the bottom is covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and in this one there is the head of the instrument; then you put your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the pipe into his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not come out, but comes until the nose; and now the nose will drain, and if it doesn’t drain, then start the fumigation again many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and chew salty things and others, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary that it is cured by this government. 
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the gums is, when one can see it, like tongs bent so as to enter into the throat; and it has the appearance of a bird's beak, and it has asperities of lime, so that when it takes hold, it cannot let go; and behold here the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscesses are, according to what memory comes later in this book, both one and the other; and they differ in perforation and size; and it is in two ways which one is in its own likeness, and from that which it holds moisture. 
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the limbs which are on the body. 
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the abscess of the head is other than that of the foundation, and the abscess of the fleshy part is other than that which comes in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.  
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if to abscesses one should not pierce until the boil is ripe according to its completion; and if to some it befits to pierce when they are crusty and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses which are near joints.  
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near the joints, and it is left until it is completely rotten, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb. 
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Ou the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay the perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the principal member; where it is near the base, then pierce it so that it is ripe; and it is not fitting that you pierce an abscess without complete digestion, except for the one which is near the base, lest it become too long and open inward, and there comes a fistula; and cannot heal in a great time.  
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of the perforation of the abscess which is mature according to its completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the fever has decreased, and the lessening of the pain and redness, and of the swelling and softening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation where more depends the place of the abscess, and where it opens pus; and be the perforation long in the body, and whether the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all their equal places where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these that are crooked, according to which limb. 
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is worth knowing that you let the perforation remain as long as it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said.  
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before those things, then the body of the sperm will be lengthened from him, and is full of much filth; and by chance harden the lips and the depths of him. 
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if on any abscess that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb needs. 
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must make small abscesses in small abscesses, small incisions; and in large abscesses, large incisions, and many cuts according to the semblance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cover the heart, and to cover; when it has become as thick as cloth, and is closed, you must do as with boils: and if there are such that are cut in III angles, and if there are such as are covered like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of the angles; and if there are such where one makes a round incision, and other sizes and similar incisions. 
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Whoever has no chief, such as a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it thoroughly; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has gathered much pus, and you pierce it, if you do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but drain part of it; then stop the abscess until the next day, then drain nothing further; do this many times little by little, until the pus is all gone; same thing if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman carrying, or young children, or old men decrepit. 
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes twists with the exit of the gut, which by chance kills the patient, and you do not lose heart. 
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid therefore this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, so wipe the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a plain cut, administer tents of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, it is necessary that you put in each one a tent so that it comes one against the other; and if you have cut into the abscess a piece of skin, and you have covered it inside, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or lint shavings of linen without moisture, and tie it until the third day; then remove the bandage, and cure it with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood flow happens in your work, then administer cold water and thus, moisten the cloth, and place it on the bleeding spot many times. 
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the flow of blood persists, administer governance and care to it, and the powders that I have said in this book with your hands, and if it is in winter time, and the wounds or abscesses are very nervous, then it is necessary that you put on tents and cloths softened in wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the wound is fleshy, then it is necessary that you put on cloths softened in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then untie the abscess and wipe it and cure it, as it befits, until it is healed. 
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what one must know universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where the heart of the head come small abscesses, and are manner of us that are in cloths, like as the joints of a gherkin, and much in it of likenesses.   
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and such that have moisture as well as pulses; and there are some that are hard and stony at the waist, and there is no doubt if the artery does not work against it. 
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the waist is that you provide to all the instrument which is called "enteroscopist," because its form comes here after, what thing it contains. 
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then cover it from above with a long cloth.  
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is dried, then peel away without leaving the hair that contains that moisture, because it returns back when one leaves it alone; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and wine, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and remove what remains of the pus. 
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then begin again the cotton, as before, the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain of the pain; then cure the wound with ointment as is fitting, until it is healed. 
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds in the flesh, so cut it according to this form, long; and throw your forceps there, and the scab from all sides, and put all your care into drawing out the pus where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, then do what I have told you afterwards. 
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do with an abscess if it is foul, and of cutting and curing as I have told you. 
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the tail on the purulent abscess and the moist one is lighter because they are of little blood. 
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if to some of these abscesses or chiefs where there is no moisture, and of these former abscesses that I copied or chief of an old woman; and found the abscess as a hard stone, rough and white, and cannot break; and if one had done any, one would have done him as well a wound as with a stone. 
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or chief, for that which come at the top of children and the roots of the ears, the opening should be always at the most dependent place, in order to let out the pus; and the cure as it is fitting. 
des scrophules	Of the scrofulous
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur at the neck, and under the arms, and in the groins, and sometimes they come elsewhere on the body, and are numerous, and interlaced with one another. 
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its side, as the nodule and abscess of the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofulas are many.  
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some who contain moisture, and there are some who do not want to obey health. 
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that which you see of good disposition in the touch, and similar to the color of the body, and mute from each side and is not a bit fierce to the nerves of the neck nor to the artery nor to the conduit, and is not too deep; then it befits you to cut it from above, and to scrape it from each part, and extend the two lips of the heart as incisions, if you have need for it, like as we have said in abscesses of the head; and treat little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and be not the spatula too sharp or trenching, that the hand does not slip, and do not see too far forward, that you do not cut what you should not. 
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, then put in the wound powdered vitriol, or some powders that restrain blood, and hold the wound; and leave it until the abscess is appeased, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot. 
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is cleansed, return to your work, until you complete it; then carefully examine with your index finger if there remain any small scabs, and cut them and remove them.  
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a vein in the root of the scrofula large, then it does not behoove you to cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a double strong thread, and let it hang by it, without causing pain; then apply the wound of old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then cure it.  
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut all of the scrofula, it is necessary that you assemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, since there is no delay of superfluity for the size of the scrofula.  
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If it is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it, and milk furred, and cut as we have said. 
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that hold superfluity, pierce there where it appears more; and pierce thus as that before said, depending, then administer ointments with similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, then the cure of ointment bringing forth flesh, until it is healed.  
de squinance	Of squinting
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen in our land who did it, and this is the scripture of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinance, it is necessary that the slit of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be cut; and one should not help them with this because all the veins and arteries of the patient are hot at those who have an abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in two almonds.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the artery, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the perdition that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary when we want to cut the epiglottis that we cut it below III circles or IV a small incision through the, between the II circles or by the quantity of the incision of the syfac, not in the cartilage; and this its so suitable for the section of the epiglottis that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long enough. 
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he extend the skin of the throat to all the spine, then fends the heart as far as it comes to the channel; and escape the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then cut the syfac, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm of the channel that salt is thrown out from the place which is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open a piece. 
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour is past because one doubts the strangulation, assemble the .ij. lips of the wound of the heart, and sew all alone sense the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, as long as it is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says that one should not do this juice until the throat is completely stopped up and the patient is judged to be dead and the lack is in the wing.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, cover the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe and they breathe through the wound, and thus are kept from death; and for this reason, ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it passes in III days or in IIII. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw. 
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young woman took a knife and stabbed it in her throat, and cut part of the channels of the windpipe; and I was called by her to cure her, and I found her as dead. 
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that was coming from it, and I well know that it had not been cut to a vein nor led anywhere but to the throat, and the veins were passing through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I bandaged it, and thus I healed the wound, until it was cured; and did not happen to the maiden that she would be hoarse, and returned after to her disposition; for this reason I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis is no fear. 
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "throat hernia," and it is a large abscess in the color of a boil, and it is mostly in women; and it is according to II manners: natural, and accidental; where natural has no cause. 
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident is according to II manners, of which one is similar to fat us, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery; and there is fear, and it does not become to work to do outside than in this one that is small, and proves and searches all the introduction: if you find it as I am fat, and cannot at any vein, so cut it, as we cut the us, and the train to all its coat, if there is any; and encircle well quickly, and cure it as it befits, until it is perfectly healthy. 
des nous	of ours
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways to us, which I will tell all the likenesses; and now it befits me to say all the difference that is between our and outcome. 
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that others is sometimes and fever-holding, as long as the boils are passed, and is completed the corruption; therefore rests the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new one there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and contains it its own sack and is according to the color of the body, and begins also as a boil, and becomes big; and are according to two appearances, or fatty, or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.  
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the wound, that you first examine and inquire about all the instrument which is called "intropositor," according to its form or chapter which is after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquisiting the abscesses by us is that you prick or more moist place that you find in the abscess, and turn your two points and points, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess; then extract the introducer, and take care in those that jump out may. 
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the moisture runs short, what color it has, do as I have said of other abscesses; and if after the introducer there comes no moisture, know that it is fat, so make it in a cross, and take it with tweezers, and scrape it lightly on each side and ward the coat where it lies so that you draw it out clean with the needle; and if you cannot draw it out clean, then draw it by pieces so that nothing remains.   
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	Car if it remains nothing there, it returns to us many times; and if it remains a little bit, and the patient does not grieve, then apply some corrosive powders to the wound, and restrain the wound, and put on soothing things above an ointment hot, and cure it with other cures until it is healed; and if the lump is large, then cut the two lips of the wound, and cure it with what generates flesh. 
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein pulsating is against you or otherwise hurry and apply the place of pulverized vitriol, and let it lie for two days or three, until the wound festers, and repose the boiling of blood; then return to copper what is remaining of the out.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of the instruments for inserting, and they are in 3 ways: great and medium and small; and there are 3 squares that are called "albaret", and 1 that is called "breb", and there are in 3 ways: great, medium, and small, to surround the abscesses of fistula; and they are also like needles with which one sews the sorceresses, and they are of citrine iron or silver, and those who are yellow are worth more, and they are more proven by black flint to surround the curves of fistula; and they are in 3 ways: great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the breadth of the openings.  
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of tweezers are of many resemblances, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are tweezers that have two curves in three ways also; and there are tweezers that have three curves, and they are also in three ways; and there are tweezers that have two curves, and tweezers of a single curve only, and they are in three ways; and all of these are necessary in their place. 
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these things is to be cut, and there are some that do not cut more than one side, which we scrape the skin for; so that one does not cut the vein nor the nerve; and among these instruments are the alemeles put back in handles, so that the patient does not feel them at the opening of abscesses; and they are of III manners: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one does not use them except in fleshy parts, such as legs, arms, breasts, and armpits, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another instrument small, resembling a fist, according to this form, for which one drains blood. 
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one puts it sometimes in the place that heals with incision of veins, and arteries, and sometimes re-enters according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to rot, until they resemble female breasts; and remain discolored and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, it is necessary to follow this form from this line .b. up to .g.. 
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scrape the fat, and apply medicine to the wound preventing flesh, then assemble the two lips of the wound together with stitching, and cure it until it is healed; and if it swells downwards, and softens as it happens to women, make it in two ribs above, by two similar cuts; so that one holds onto the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to the line .g.; then scrape the skin which is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and there administer what we have said of stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or for the blood loss, then it behooves you to fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it softens the remaining and the fat, then cure it until it is healed. 
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the buttocks are types of hard scrofulous ulcers or boils and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line .b. to the line .g.:
