Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is emptied, then apply to the wound old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and care with ointment following this until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to boils, then treat it as we have said for incisions of boils, and if the wound returns with pus, then apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is wounded, and the skin is sutured which is on top, there often come abscesses, and just as well it happens to the vein swollen and abscess; and if you know it's for the artery, then the abscess is long in making; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel a tightening; and when it is for the vein, it appears red from being inflamed; and it is foolishness to cover this abscess, and even when it is under the armpits and around the neck and at many other places, and is very large.  
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It behooves then to seek the cure of iron, and whoever is at the chief behoove as well, and in that one who is inflamed by artery making from above the skin long; then work the size as incisions, and depart beautifully the artery from the cloths, so long as it is discovered; then put under it a needle, and make it pierce until the other side, and restrain the artery with a double thread in II lengths, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the II arteries which are in temples; then point the place that is between the II links of a trocar as long as the blood that is there, and be relieved the abscess; then administer the cure that engenders bowe, so long as the thread hangs; then cure those of ointment coming to those, until it is healed; and if the abscess is for the size of the vein, then it behoove you to hold in your hand what you can of the abscess to all the skin, then put the needle under the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and there be the double thread, so that you draw it from the other side; then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or thread of one of II parts as II heads of the thread; and if you doubt that the threads are not issued, then put another needle to all the thread under all the abscess to the incision of the first needle, and restrain the threads in IIII lengths; then cut the abscess so long as the superfluities are issuing, then cut the superfluity of the skin and leave what is tied; then put on top the cloth moistened in wine and oil, then administer them cures of tents and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also as abscesses come in the artery and in the vein, abscesses come to the nerves when they are injured, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often to shoulders and hips and in all the places where there are joints, and it is a grief abscesses, and its color seems the color of the body, and it is in many dispositions without pain; and when one constrains it, the patient feels pain, and is not quite in accordance with the body, but below the heart; and moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, neither down nor up, and the one that is in the joints should not be covered with iron: lest there may be contraction; and the one who is on the head or on the forehead, makes the skin to the spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, then hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root; and if it is large, then suspend it with a bandage, and scrape it, then remove the pus and assemble the wound with sutures, and treat it until it is healed. 
des grosses boces pendans	of great boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it occurs in the belly and nowhere else; and is a disease which is called «fungus» because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and are the roots subtle, and the head large; and there are some small and very large; and I saw the man who had two in his belly which were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had fine roots, and they were slightly split, and moisture flowed out of them.  
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them and found in one XVIII ounces weighing, and in the other VI З., and the work in incision so that you look if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is pale and moist and of subtle root; if the cut to the spatula wide, and be in your presence the cautery to the fire. 
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the waist often come great hemorrhages and if the blood does not stop quickly then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and afraid of the incision of iron, take a thread of flax well made, and tie it in the artery as we have said, and let it remain for days; and then restrain it, and do not cease restraining the thread of flax until it cuts off the artery, and comes to an end by itself without working; and if the roots are large, fear to cut even for the belly, but you may well cut half, then cauterize that it does not return; then cure the wound, and keep that you do not cut the thread which is of pale color and poor sense and of milk secretion. 
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is a boil, inflamed, and I shall come to its treatment later on.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the blister has become full
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from cautery of a wound or cut of the flesh, and is on the belly and in some cases of the boils, as they happen in other ruptures, or of blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is before, or of wind; and if it is through the rupture of the flesh and by the issue of the boil, then the color of the abscess seems like the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and open of diverse exit.  
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is for the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it at its ends it rises, and then returns, and perhaps it is scarred, and enlarged much at the entrance of the bath and for hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is for moisture, it is a light thing, and open well when you press it with your hand, nor constrain it at all; and if it is for blood, then it opens by these signs the abscesses large and hard, and are fixed according to a quantity; and if it is for windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the work is that you look whether its appearance is for the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness. 
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	So it is proper that you leave the care. 
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear in it, as I have told you in this chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.  
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the bowel, then it befits that you command the patient to hold his arm, and let it be stretched straight, then sign all around the belly; then command him to seize firmly between your hands, then go around the place that you have signified to the whole spatula, then extend half of the abscess above to the entire great incision; then tie it around with a strong thread, or a cord of strong silk firmly, and let the wound be bound by the linen; then operate the half of the abscess extended on the linen, and put your index finger in, and seek the intestine; if you find it caught in the linen, then untie it, and put the intestine outside of the belly; and if you find the bowel, then take it at the incision, and cut away the superfluity; and if the artery makes it contrary to you, or the vein, then go beautifully around, then return to your work and take II needles, and put II through threads, and put the II needles around that which you have made in a cross as you make it perceive; then strain the abscess in IIII places on the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave the place as long as it will rot, and let the dead flesh decay by itself; or you cut it when it is subtle and rotten, then cure it of what is necessary, and heal the abscess as we have said; and drain the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place of what is necessary, and suture the place.
dou chancre	Of the ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the likenesses of an ulcer, and how one must work on it by medicines, and how one must avoid the cure of iron; and let us say that the ulcer is generated in the marshes, and great caution should be exercised in its cure, and the ancients said that when a chancre is in a place where one can scrape it away like a chancre that is in the armpits, and in the groin, and similar places, and it must all be removed when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, then it does not behoove you to approach it, for I have never been able to heal any of them; nor has anyone ever healed any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge the patient once of black bile; then let him bleed if there is manifest repletion, then make the patient's  good place to perform the work; then throw your curette or ulcer, and shave it on all sides, and ossify it on all sides without leaving anything; and allow the blood to flow out completely, and press well on the place with your hand or any thing, and if the bleeding from the incision of the artery or vein is against you, then cauterize it as long as the blood is extinguished; then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have just said in the division the likenesses of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each likeness, and the cure which is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron; so it is only lit; and one should not touch iron in these two likenesses: that is to say, tympanites and hydrops arche, because it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicate this likeness of dropsy which is called "lit" by medicines, and the cure does not profit, see if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as cough and solution of the belly and similar things; if one does not touch iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other illness besides dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must work thus: lift the patient straight up on your hands, and the ministers press the belly pushing the water to the lowest part under the ribs, then take the spinal spatula according to this form: 
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be trenchant of the two parts. 
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	At the point, and yet do not go in so far that it can come to the intestine when you put it in, and do not pierce it; then look if the dropsy is near the intestines: if it should be, cut into it above the belly III two right below the nipple; and if the dropsy is because of the liver disease, then make your incision on the left side of the belly III two; and if it is because of the spleen, then on the right, and do not let the patient lie on the incision so that the superfluities run to that weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and put it in, and lift your hand throughout the spatula between the skin and the fascia as much as when you are scraping a quantity of an ungle or more; then pierce the fascia until the spatula comes to the place eight, and this is the level of the water, then pull the thread out, and put this instrument back from what here is the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a silver needle, and is of iron or light bronze, and in the lower part there is one small hole; and on one side there are three holes; and two on the other; and one on the other; and the head is cut like a pen, and this is the form of the incision with which scribes cut the pen.  
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the head above is the alemele, so that when the instrument comes to the point, it descends now on the instrument; empty therefore half or a third part, for if you empty more than is fitting in that hour, perhaps the patient dies for the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls unconscious, or he approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulses; then treat the instrument and retain the point, and it is retained now by the heart which stops the passage that is on the syfac, because I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then begin the instrument the other day, if you see the patient suffering from it, and treat of the point a small quantity; do this any day, and keep yourself from flowing until there remains no more than a bit of point. 
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and you let him drink a lot of water, so treat with burial or hot sand, and with much sweat or bath and in the sun, and keep him from drinking; and treat with drying medicines until he is cured, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before. 
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who have no opening in their penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its place. 
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If this is appropriate then he shall be able to see through the whole spatula very delicately according to this form. 
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put or pierced I the small plug of plank, and tie it and keep it so III days or IIII and when he wants to make urine, be it removed the plug, and do urine, and then put it back; and by adventure he does not need it, because the urine that comes forward does not leave it closed. 
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He whose wound is small, so is medicated with the cloth of plan, as we have said, and it will widen.  
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the foreskin in its place are pale because none are born with the foreskin at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate until they lift their penis up; and cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot come to the urethra, and it is a bad disease. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is that the patient lies often on his back, and the head of the penis and the scrotum are extended as long as a feather, so that the hole falls in the middle, as it should; and keep watch for blood loss which often comes, and if it happens, let the stanch who stanches blood do so, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pimples of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these blemishes come on the penis, and is an appearance of ugly flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so it is necessary that you prick them with i. one fine needle, and scrape and clean all, then put cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment; then cure with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the abscess is malignant, of bad color and pus-filled, then it is necessary that you bring a cautery to it. 
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have captured it, and if the splint is in some the staff, and has part inside the skin and part outside, then it behoves that you remove the splint that is inside first; and when it is healed, then care for the outside. 
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, if the head of the shaft is not made sure that it is pierced, and blackening and corruption come in its shaft and where the opening; so it befits to shear everything that is black and corrupted, then put on top the plaster of honey and flour which is made of bark of wild quince and vines, then treat it with other dressings until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, administer the lunar cautery according to this form: 
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps with two things: that is to say, for drawing blood and for corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you put or conduct on the penis a cane of lead, and piss the patient among; and when the skin is raised at the head of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or where there is a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary that you scrape it with the instrument called "cheveit" until the ligaments are untied, and the head of the penis is delivered from all sides; and if it is a painful thing to consider this, it is necessary that you scrape it with the spatula any point at the head of the penis and the skin; then separate well between them, and put between them the fine veil of linen moistened in cold water so that it does not raise. 
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not of the healing kind like other wounds; however, when we perform this work by our will and properly on children, it becomes necessary that we do the best work, and the easiest to heal.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcision for their children, because they did not practice it in their law, and we have more than what we acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I wanted the most part of the masters and surgeons who did circumcisions near .i. dal, and as forces, and with a whole novacule; so fuioit the keurs because there are .ij. cloths, and perhaps if one cuts the above and leaves the below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or it is convenient to cut, and the pain is doubled, and to the purification which is due dal it is not assured the point of the member; and to the purification of the angle perhaps the iron escapes, and runs the work, and many times they are born as if they do not need purification and I have wanted.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the purification which is done with force to all the line of thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, because the forces cut justly as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, make it even in I all stretch; but that the thread be well wrapped around the skin; and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child think, if he understands, that you are only tying the thread around the phallus just so, and then let him jump around in all the ways he can; then make him lie between your hands straight, and support the forces between your hands or under your feet that the child does not see them, nor any of the tools; then put your hand to the phallus and blow or heart, and pull it up until the head of the phallus is in; then clean it well of the dirt that is assembled there, then tie the place sign with a double thread, then tie it below I pock at the other lien; and hold it as II two by the second lieure to the pouch and to the index finger, and cut between the II liens, then raise the heart upwards gently and pull the head of the phallus; then let the blood flow drop by drop, for that is the cure; and put powder on and on top of the powder I drape it with a cloth of an egg cooked destempreit d’aigue rose, mixed with good and fresh rose oil, and let it lie there until the next day, and cure him from other cure until he is healthy.  
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces at the fortification is this: the two shoulders be held and be sharp, and the shoulders also as big as the hands equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the fortification is when the kernels inside are at the incision; therefore it behooves you to extend it to your finger, so that the lesions make an abscess; and cut equally, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then take pliers, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pierce .iij. days, and that which is below the shaft is swollen, leave it until the abscess heals, and gently scrape it; then cut it as much as you can move, and guard yourself from the part of the shaft, it will do it no harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the place of things suddenly wound with powder, which we have said or treated of powders, and if you cut beyond measure the kernel, and it goes upwards, it will do no harm; cure therefore it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to the stone in the bladder or blood congealed, or bowel, or new flesh, or similar things, that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see the retention because of the stone which is at the root or neck of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bent on his knees; and the feet should be placed on the back, and extend the belly from above the back, and restrain the patient's legs as much as he can; and then the neck of the bladder is constrained to the expression of the stone upwards, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary that you administer extraction with all the instrument which is called "syringe", of which this is the form: and be of fine silver light capped, like the feather of a bird; and let the shaft be half a palm long, and be fine at the tip. 
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the issue of urine is that you take the double thread and tie it to the head of the wool or cotton piece, and put the head of the thread inside the syringe; and cut the superfluity of the wool and put it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and rue of egg, and make the patient sit on the seat, and raise the bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and tepid water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis, until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis from above towards the bud; then push the syringe forward until it reaches the bladder, and let the patient feel it come to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order for that which leads or where it goes is twisted; then hold the thread at all the wool piece and piece, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it, and make correct the urine; and restart the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is aligned. 
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When sores or blood comes in the bladder, or there is assembled rotting, and you see it distilling sharp waters and medicines, so do to all the instrument which is called "clepsedre", and that is the form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has III openings: II on one side, and I on the other, as you see; and the leaus (cheves) because of which the medicine should be such that it well stops the rod without addition, so if one can drain the moisture, and push when necessary; and when you see fit to put your medicines in the bladder, put the chief of the speculum in the moisture, and draw with the syringe that is inside; so draw the moisture to the speculum, and then firmly replace the syringe inside; so will the moisture enter inside, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle enema by which one enemas the bladder: so it is here.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or of copper, and the head is higher; and below to the chest where the ligaments fall; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the moisture which you see to enema the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts with a good strong double thread, and heat the point of the enema on the fire; then insert the tip of the enema into the anus, then strain your hand on the bladder throughout the entire administration of the moisture, until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you don't have the bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make it in a circle, and pierce it roundly all around; then put a strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a dial, and put inside that which you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder. 
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the manners of stone, and the extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone engendered as rains, and all the signs, and in what stone one must work of size; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you it openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder often happens to children, and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder seeming like water in its subtlety; and it appears hareng, and hardens the patient's penis, and he can many times, and then urinates; and with many of these jumps the foundations are formed; and it is light the healing of children until they have 4 years, and it is very grievous in old men, and it is as the middle for those who are between childhood and old age; and the cure is lighter from those who have the large stone, than from those who have the small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient by enema, to draw out all the phlegm that is in the intestines. 
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hampers seeking out the stone.  
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and push them out and move them downward, so that the stone descends to the opening of the bladder, and sometimes comes out from its high place; then make him sit between your hands properly arranged, and his hands be below his thighs, so that the bladder is entirely inclined downward; then feel and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then haste now to cut above the stone. 
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall to the touch of all, moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is a young man; and put it in its foundation, and seek the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, bring it to the neck of the bladder; then press upon it with your finger, and put it out on the outside where you see fit to cut. 
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister that he presses the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the testicles upward, and with his left hand remove the skin which is below the testicles in the part where one makes the incision; then put the spatula cutting, for this is its form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make between that which is between the hips and the foundation, not in the middle but at the side of the left hip; and be straight on top of the stone, and your two sides should be wide or foundation, and let the tailpiece be so wide as for it to be wide outside, and inside narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; by chance the press those who are at or foundation, that she may jump out without work; and know that there is such a stone where it has angles, and margins: if it is grated to issue; and if there is one that is smooth, resembling a gland, and round, whose outlet is light.  
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	To him then where there are angles and margins, make the cut larger; and if it does not come out, it is necessary that you pull up with pliers which are also like a file at the head, so as to force the stone out so that it does not escape; or you put underneath the subtle instrument curved at the head; and if you cannot manage it this way, then widen the hole of the opening, and if it is hard, restrain it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, first put in the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut up, then pull out the larger, and after that the smaller ones if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, then it should be treated, and a larger wound made. 
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine comes back through where the urethra cannot close; but nonetheless, you force to drain it, or to tear it with tweezers, until you pull it in pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound of incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and restrain it, and put on top the cloth moistened in oil and wine, or in rose water and cold water, to appease the hot abscess; then bind the patient on his neck, and do not untie the bandage until the third day. 
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, moisten the place well with oil and water, then treat it with diaphania ointment and basilicon ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if an abscess comes in the wound and corrosions, and congealing of blood in the bladder, and by this is retained the urine, which is known in such manner that without jumping with the urine: then you do in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains there, it will corrupt the bladder, and burn it; then lift the wound of water and of ash and of silk, and help him in all the ways that you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that all the hours that you cure him, that you bind his two thighs, and assemble the medicines on the spot. 
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is where the urethra leads, and it is stuck there, and the urine cannot pass; so the cure of those that I say thus, that you cut it many times, is excused from the cutting by this cure. 
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this thus.  
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one piece of iron according to this form and have it made with three angles on one stick:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the rod below the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then push the forest into the rod gently, until it reaches the stone; and turn the forest with your hand in the stone poke and poke, as long as you can feel the stone on the other side; soon will come the urine, then press your hand upon what remains of the stone which is within the rod. 
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is immediately broken, and jump out with the urine, and the patient heals; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie I thread under the stone and the other above, then making the rod right on top of the stone between the two threads, then extract it, and untie the thread, and purify the frozen blood which is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed. 
de la piere des femmes	of the women’s stones
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that stones are engendered in women, and if it happens at any time, it is the grief of cure, and it is forbidden for three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman well knowing who exposes herself to the mires, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more deep than the stone of the man, for which it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and great fear there is. And if necessity demands this, it is necessary that you choose a midwife well knowing, and by force find one, and if you do not find one, do not so much as ask; cast mire subtle; and present her with a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command her of the investigation of the stone; and look well whether the woman is virgin: then it is necessary to put her loin or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, constrain her below her loin, and recommend that she put her loin or with the patient, and seeks and presses her left hand on the bladder forming. 
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, then it is necessary that she move it from great to great from the entrance of the bladder down to below, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut upon the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the buttock, where it appears pushed out, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her foot above the stone or below, and let the tail be at first small; then push the point into the waist, if you feel the stone so much on the wound as the stone can pass out, and know that many kinds of stones are: that is to say, small and large and rough and smooth, long and rounded, and which have veins.  
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the likenesses to know the outcome. 
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the stone should not come out, put crushed vitriol on it and hold it for an hour until the stone is softened; then return to your work, as long as the stone remains firm, and have the instruments that I told you in extracting stones from men to help you in your work; and if the stone does not come out, and it is an artery that is cut, put the powder on the place and strain it with bandages, and do not start over, and leave the stone and do not drain it, for fear of killing the patient; then cure the wound. 
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased, and the tissues are healed, then return to your work as long as the stone is weak.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing else than a gathering of moisture or white syfac, which is the substance under the shell of eggs, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac," and sometimes is properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that it is another egg; and this is the skin of the egg between the white syfac that we have said; and these do not have any other part.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this ramice is so weak that it comes from the eggs, and is spread out that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: either declining to jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or aqueous white, and this happens more; and these are the signs of knowing this assembly, because if it is white as we have said, then the abscess is ripe, I long like the figure of an egg, and does not open the joints, because it has moisture all around. 
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the skin itself, then the abscesses redden with a part of the yolk, and for that reason it is thought to be another yolk; and if the moisture is between the skin of the scrotum and the white syfac, then one feels it well; therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, you should examine the entire intropositor quarreit, for its form is as above. 
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this therefore which comes after the introducer, judge of this which is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his ability and the filling of his body; then place him on his back, on something a little high, and put under him a lot of cloths; then he sits on his left side, and commands the minister that he sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the heart of the sides; then take the spatula, and cut the skin of the sides among them as long as up to the armpit, and let your incision be straight in dividing the skin of the sides until the white fat, and exfoliate subtly according to your ability; then pierce the fatty layer full of water with a large opening, and extract all the water, and then put your dressings, and place the fatty layer above; and do not touch the heart of the sides, but only the fatty layer; cut all or in pieces equally the costal side of him subtly, that if you don't cut it well carefully, it will return the water; and if the work has gone wrong, put it back in its place when you have finished the work of the fatty layer; then assemble the two leaves of the heart of the sides with a suture, then cure it like the other wounds, until it is healed. 
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the sheaf corrupted by another illness, then it befits that you tie the vessels that are suspended, in doubting the discharge of blood; then cut the stone to all the suspender, and extract the sheaf, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the wound is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; so cut the other part as you have done the first evenly, then wipe the blood, and put on the wound a layer of wool soaked in rose oil; and put above the two piles a layer of wool soaked in wine and oil, and put bandages over them, and tie it with a bandage all along according to this form: 
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two pieces of cloth and employ them with woolen padding according to this semblance and let them be assembled by stitching in the crotch of the breeches, and one of the chiefs pricks above the foundation to the back, and the other at the armpit part; and the other of the chief over the two shoulders, and let the whole restraint be assembled in the buckle of the bracer; and sometimes is medicine this twig of cautery instead of iron size, and it is that you prick the cautery dagger subtle, and cut the skin of the testicles, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white syrup containing the water is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that syrup at once, and scorch it with this subtle hot cautery. 
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cap in all ways that you can, as long as you sear everything; and keep that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more salve; and moves guarding against bleeding, and measures that the works of size; and if anything makes contrary to you, or abscess chaws or bleeding or other thing, so cure what makes contrary to you, according to what is said before. 
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful, and does not want to wait for this work because of its horror, so administer a perforation, as I tell you, and it is that when you are well certain by the significations that we have said that watery root is there, so make the patient sit on the raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below all the spatula wide, and put the perforation long from the body; and let the punctures be wide, so that all the water flows; then put cotton on the place, and tie it, and leave to drain the remaining of the water, then cure it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to flow out at the mouth of the wound, so you should put a quill or the instrument that one treats the water of the dropsy, of which the form is before; and enlarge the place of the wound, and know that the water returns, and it is assembled after six months or until then, and when it is assembled as before, and thus will pass the days of the patient. 
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the section of this branch there is fear in many dispositions, so it seems to me better to leave it; and I will tell you the work and appearances of the abscess. 
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come to the body, and also to the joints; and this is by many causes.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to know by superfluity sour and acute, which is spread to the groin, or from percussion; and it is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and does not find any pain, and is a grievous abscess; and perhaps there are some abscesses grievous fearsome and stony, and of dusky color, and sometimes comes from our artery, or swelling of vein. 
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from an artery, it is known by the arrangement of a hot abscess, when you press it with your hands; and it is not right that you touch it. 
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of vein inflation is known by his disposition to the expression of the touch of the fingers, and can well do the size on this likeness, and on the other arms; and that you cut the heart of the veins, then being the egg on top, and the train of the white thereof, and deliver the suspenders from all parts of the egg. 
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already cooked with these new dishes, then you must pull out the yolk, and cut it; and if it is in the yolk sac, or in what is inside the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver all that membrane, and cut it roundly.  
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is or its rear, then it behooves you to cut it completely, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your works are accomplished, then apply the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then cover it with other dressings until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a covering resembling the border, with the softening of the edges, and the patient moves painfully when he walks; and the cure for this illness is as well frightening as the one before, but nonetheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It behooves you to have the patient sit on an elevated seat, then bind the suspender of the reins down to his hips, over all the vessels that are near the penis, and thread them together with the masters, and stretch them out; then cut into the vessels with a sharp spatula in a wide furrow throughout the vessels, until they are uncovered, and then peel from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples; then insert a needle where the vein has come, and tie it to the first place where the vein came, and tie it straight to the other end; then cut them in the middle directly, according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted humors; then cure the wound as with the others where you want to heal the flesh, so that no vessel spills that nourishes one of the reins; for by these none comes harm, and if to all the vessels blood comes, it behooves to draw the reins to all the vessels; so that the testicle does not lose its nourishment because of the incision of the vessels, and dries up and cannot be aided. 
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the sinew
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The events of this branch are by the section that comes or where it is extended on the belly in the part of the angles, so that the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the corners; and this rupture is either at the site of the syphax, or of the extension of it, and come these II manners of mouth from causes: either by percussion, or by jump, or by braying, or by lifting of heavy load, and by similar things; and the signs when it is of the extension of the syphax, is that there are pops and pops, over a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are equal up to the height of the navel, because the syphax presses the intestines.  
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of the pus, that it brings at the beginning sudden pain, and the abscess is various appearances, under the skin near, and this because of the issue of the intestine and the body to the outside of the pus.
