Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes it descends the edges with the pus, and is held in, and causes great pain to suffer the patient, even when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron there is fear, so it should be avoided.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the work is that you instruct the patient to bring the intestine back into his hand inside the wound, if he can enter it; then be careful on his neck between your hands, and raise the hips; then hold the heart above, and cut all the skin of the groin long; then put within the folds of the waist needles according to what you need to open the wound, and let it be such that the eyes can issue; then scrape the syfac that is below the skin of the groin, until the white syfac hard is uncovered on all sides; then put your index finger into what follows the groin, in what is between the white syfac which is under the skin of the womb, and between the second syfac, and depart from what is behind the womb, and between the second syfac; and then move with the right hand inside the heart of the groin, and hold the white syfac on top to your left hand, and raise the womb onto all the syfac towards the waist; and command the minister that he extend the womb upwards, and untie what is behind the ligament; and inquire with your fingers if there is any intestine surrounded or white syfac hard, and if you find any of these things, put it into the belly below; then take a needle which has a thick thread made of X threads, and put it in the back part of the syfac, which is after the skin of the groin; after the waist, then cut the hairs that appear of the threads, until there are IIII threads; then assemble them one on top of the other in the manner of a cross, and tie the syfac, about which we have said that it is below the skin of the groin, with a strong thread of II parts; then wrap the hairs of the threads, and tie them together of II parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter inside, except the abscess may come; and put straight the thread according to the first long thread II fingers of it, and after these II threads leave the syfac which is below the heart of the groin the large one of a finger; and after all the others according to the roundness that the womb carries; then cut in the part which is below the skin of the groin, as much as the scar, and the bow, as we have said before; then administer wool soaked in oil, and put it into the wounds, and put in the thread that we have said. 
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And no time is cauterized the white suture that we have said, after the incision, out of fear of blood flow.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and leave the thread as long as it hangs by itself; and if it is slow to heal, then be raised with hot water, and put on what we have said, until it heals; then treat the wound with other remedies, until it is perfectly healed. 
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this treatise I never saw anyone who dared to cure it with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made like the branch which is assembled with the twig, in such a manner that you tie the vessels, after the cut above or lightly below; then cut in the middle, and care for the abscess of those who work, until the vessels flow; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.  
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture comes in the bowels, as we have said, and opens the entrails; and do not let any of the intestines go into the anus, and if any do go out, it is small, and repairs all hours; and anyway if it stays too long in this point, then the wound or abscess grows, until the intestine comes out; and this happens because of the extension of the abscess which is in the bowels, as we have said, because it is extended, then it softens and swells the entrails and opens; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner: and that is that the patient lies lying on his back between your hands, then cut the place of the rupture inflated with a wide according to the quantity of III finger widths; and then draw out the abscess which is under the skin that goes inside, then take the root and put it on the place appearing of the abscess; and press it at the bottom of the belly, then sew the two places appearing of the abscess onto the head of the root, and sew one and the other; then remove the head of the root, and do not cut the abscess nor extend the bowel or anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the ramification of the bowels; then cure by the cure of wounds. 
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, then cover and care for the wound until it is healed. 
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The sifac is constrained, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is moved in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles softens in some men, because the sacs that are inside are softened, and it is made visible; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the patient lie on his back, and one cuts the skin that is softened on the natural skin; then assemble the two lips with a suture, and if you see, sew first the superfluity of the softened skin at three sutures or four firmly; then cut between the sutures, and treat the wound as other wounds, until it is healed, and pull out the thread.
dou chastrement	of chastisement
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that cauterization is common in our law, and for this reason I would like to not speak of it in this book; and it is necessary only for two reasons: one of which is that the wise may answer when asked about it, and know how to cure it; and the other, because we often need cauterization of some animals to aid us, such as goats and sheep and cattle and other beasts. 
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I therefore say that fastenings are made in two ways: either by traction, or by fending. 
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by traction, make the animal sit in hot water, until the joints are softened and pliable; then grasp them with your hand, until they are set and you no longer feel them. 
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the chastisement of the tail: It behooves you to hold the beast, and press the skin of the scrotum with your left hand, then tie the suspender, and cut above each ear at the time, when you have well scraped them; and leave no prick on it or the subtle prick that is on the vessels; and this manner of chastisement is better than the one done by attraction, because in attraction perhaps nothing remains from the scrotum, because the beast desires lust; then cure the wound until it is healed. 
des hermofrodites	of the hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodite is according to two manners as men: one if it is that between the two sexes opens as much as the figure of nature of a woman, or it has hair, and sometimes in short the urine.  
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is so in women, and it is above the point as well as a rod and it joins. 
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the care of man and woman is that you cauterize all the joints attached to them, and cure them as other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine flows through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure. 
de la tentigene	of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A wart is a hard growth on the natural part of the body, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the cure.  
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you remove the superfluity of the tongue with your hand or tongs, and cut it lightly; and do not cut too deeply, lest bleeding occur. Then cure it with another remedy until it is healed; and in another manner that arises at the mouth of the marsh, and the temple, and by chance happens to be, and according to its appearance like a cow, and for this reason they called it by the ancients “cow disease.” 
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to cut it, as we have said before, and care for it until it is healed. 
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or an accident by illness that came to it; or it is by cartilage attached, or by a subtle or thick syrup, and it is made in the groin, or ribs, or underarm, or wherever; and it prevents conception, and pregnancy, and perhaps the flowers to have; and the knowledge of this one is by the gaze of the belly.  
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the stoppage is near appearing, it desires to your two or to the root.  
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is sore with subtle pain, and it is near the two books, then hasten, and do this: put your two fingers together, and let the woman be on her back, legs spread; then let the two books form, until the subtle pain is gone, and the throbbing subsides; then take wool, and soak it in oil, and place it on the spot, and let the woman lie down at home every day, so that she cannot move. 
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the sty is hard and thick, then it behooves you to cut it with the spatula like the leaf of myrtle. 
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the stoppage is of flesh, suspend it to the wound and the cup; and have the medicines that staunch blood, such as dragon's blood, incense, and a mix with egg white; then administer a cloth of broad wool, so that the wound cannot close; and thus be prolonged, and administer a tent of dry linen; then be cured with other cures until it is healed. 
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marrow comes new flesh, then it is necessary to cover according to this manner, if it is not abscesses opened. 
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess that is festering in the flesh, one must not touch with fire. 
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without customary care and when hemorrhoids are old they become hardened; and we have said in the division their similarities with others and the signs and I will say here those that resolve healing.  
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the piles, when they are made into the buttocks, and do not appear to the touch, except by iron treatment.  
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the marsh, they can feel, those that can be cured. 
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then are the altelul as the tongs, and the cope at its roots, then powder upon medicines restraining blood, such as acaice and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then put her feet to the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if there comes a bleeding, so make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and gall and similar things, and then take barley flour, and the confite it with honey and aisil, and make a poultice on her back. 
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stays, it is good. 
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If this is not the case, if one applies suction cups to the back and breasts without wounding; then take linen and moisten it in juice of plantain or in juice of elder with old wine, and apply it on the spot. 
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess heals, care for its place with ointment until it is healed; and that one which is called "albathir" is red, and is similar to harsh chief, so it should be covered as I have said in the previous paragraph; and then the cure until it is healed.  
des apostemes de la marris	Abscesses of the buttocks
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come in the body, such as boils and pyogenic abscesses and herpes and whitlows and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and more other diseases that I have said in the division. 
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary for me to say in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the marshes, which is not like the abscesses that swell; and if you want to know the work of iron, see if the abscess is thick at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it. 
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not hasten to probe, but let him rest until the pain is calmed; and then make the patient sit on a seat, and have two small seats where he can recline, and support his back and bring his feet to the parts outside the leg; and let his hips be spread, and put his arms below his knees, and bind them well with a good band; then turn him towards the right side, and there administer the instrument that works on the mouth of the jaw, because this is how it comes in shape after; and when you see him administering this instrument, make sure he puts the point first in to know the depth of the jaw so that what goes inside the instrument does not come in too deep that it should not, and so that it does not bleed the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it must cover the depth of the jaw with cloths so that the instrument does not harm him; and make sure he puts the cone of the instrument above, and keeps holding the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and one makes it soft with one's hand, then it is necessary to cover it to the chief, to the spatula of lead; and when the boil is emptied, then it is necessary that you put in the wound tents moistened in rose oil, or in green dry oil; and put the tent further from the wound at the edge of the cavity, and put outside on the skin and on the linen cloth wet with water or mallows that are cooked; then cure afterwards for two days of ointment before this, until it is healed; and sometimes raise the skin and the wound by a clyster of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lilies and agrimony long that are cooked; then return to the ointment. 
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is returned to its place, then it is necessary that you guard yourself from cauterizing with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division. 
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The craft is first to the midwife that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman push down hard, and desire to smell the air; then the child hastens to be born; so know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and is the issue under her head, and the secondine with him; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press lightly on her belly so that the child issues quickly; because when it rises above its head, then the secondine comes with him, and the womb is freed of its superfluities by good cleansing; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. 
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes sometimes upon his feet, and comes forth the body or shoulder, and the hands, or where it comes upon his belly, or groin, and is converted by chance onto his neck, and by other bad figures; so it is necessary that the bail should be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures how one must aid them. 
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out on its head by natural issue, and the woman giving birth cries loudly, and the virtues of her are weak, then make her sit on a saddle, or the women hold her; and arose her nature d’oile or fenugreic be cooked, and then put the midwife between her thighs the small spatula whose shape is here:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the second bone, and chop at its finger until the moisture that is inside it comes out; and take the belly of the woman as long as the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to give the woman a clyster of fenugreek with sesame oil; then have her drink and sneeze of condiment, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will come out. 
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out, then it behooves you to gently push them back and forth; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman upon the seat, and raise her feet up; then throw the seat onto the ground, and hold the woman so that she does not fall during the throwing; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut off the hands with the knife which is put before, and extract the child, and reset it evenly. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the issue of the child on its feet 
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes upon its feet, it is necessary to push upwards; and then turn it back and forth, until it is even; then grasp its feet and stretch them back and forth. 
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	He jumps up to his hips if he is commanded to jump, and it makes him sneeze from the cold; if he leaps far, God willing. 
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not healed as we have said, then turn it back and forth until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For therefore it is easily remedied.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come out as we have said, then take muscillage of altee, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind all in the mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit upright until below the ribs; and when she is softened below, make her a collar of myrrh, and put it below, and let her lie for an hour; then make her sit on the seat, then make her sneeze and restrain her mouth and nose, and take her belly gently, because the child jumps now. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the issue of the child on its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, he puts his hands pocket and pocket; then it is situated on its neck, and the feet are hanging down, and lying on the bed; and folds its hands pocket and pocket, and then takes the hands on the belly, and removes the cushions below, until it is arranged down; and if the child does not jump, he takes its feet and moves them strongly, then moves the belly up, then puts his hands; and makes the child pocket and pocket; and commands to the woman that she preigne as long as the child is.   
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the birth of the child coming out with one hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to devise a way to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, make the woman get up and go; if she cannot go, make her lie on the bed and untie her legs; then administer the ointment that I have described; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on the stool, then try again to bring back the hand; and when the child is born according to its natural shape, make her sneeze and command her to hold it as long as the child is out. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of the child on its neck, and has spread its hands, and its face turned toward the back of its mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the patient hold his hand, then turn it back and forth, and the elbow slightly; and when it is even, put on the nature of the muscle above and oil, as we have said, then command him to move it back and forth; and when you have done this, let her sit on the seat, and command her to wiggle; and let her sneeze. 
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner to all of the spine
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to do this manner on the entire body, strike the body with your finger, until the moisture is drained; and if the infant leans on its face and on its neck, strike from the back, that it be not held back, and let the infant die; then put the child inside, as long as you have placed it as it should be, and command the woman to abstain any time: then it will come out easily. 
de l’issue des gemelz	of the separation of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things, and they do not live, if one knows their name; I know these, that they be multiplied, and they are seized by the syfac who divides them, which is tied to the bud; and sometimes they come out as naturally as all together, as we have said. 
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are raised high, carry out the treatment as we have said, and let the patient be subtle, and do what she does quickly and lightly; and do so until it comes to salvation. 
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the marshes I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of their sage glorious, and it is necessary that the bailiff knows all this, because by chance similar things happen; so do according to what is necessary.  
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman with the dead child or womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with your hands; so it is necessary that you know if the woman is of healthy virtue, and has no accident or she has fear of death; so it is necessary that the woman be laid on her back, and her shoulders be inclined downwards, and her legs raised; and the minister teigne her from two parts, or she is tied to the bed so that she not be moved by the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils with a poultice of altee and fenugrec and flaxseed, then oil the hands of the midwife with these oils and these poultices; then put them in the womb gently, then desire I her where she puts the instruments that be suitable to those, and take ward if the child is appeared that it descends on his head; so put the instruments in her eyes or neck or mouth or in her palate or below the beard or in the throat or near the ribs, and if the descent is on its feet, so put it in the groin and in the middle ribs; and it is necessary that she holds the instrument with her right hand, and puts the curve between her fingers of the left hand, and she puts it to all her hand gently, and puts the instrument in any one of those places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing; and this is the form of the instrument:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then place against the other bone, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions are equal; and then make them equally in moving from one side to another, to move freely, and let the bones be toothed to move hold, as this is the form: 
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains,  he anoints the bail some of his oil, and puts them in that part, and draws the other part; and if none remain, he places this one or higher than its place, and does so until it comes out completely. 
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be brought back due to tightening, it is necessary that you wrap it on the cloth, until it becomes whole; then cut into the joint of the foot or at the knee, and so it should be done with the other hand, and for the two feet.  
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and it is stuck at the exit, where there is a sharp peak assembled, then it is necessary that you insert the pointed spatula between your two, and make the chief and extract the sharp point; or you do it with the instrument which is called «almidach», so that the form comes with the instruments or chapter which is after this one; and in the same way, do it if the child has a large head naturally; and then pull the bones with pliers, and if the head jumps out and it is strained by force, then be split, as long as the moisture which is or worse exit; and if it cannot exit, then cut it into pieces at the point that you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then it is necessary that you pierce it until the moisture runs. 
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, the attraction is light, and the application to the mouth of the mare is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is in the belly or the breast, it is necessary that you extract it to the drapery wrapped on the hand; and make the belly or the breast, until the moisture which is there is corrected; and if the other members are ossified, and the head remains, then put the bail your hand into the marrow; and pull it up to the mouth of the marrow; then put the pin or two, and pull it further; and if the mouth of the marrow is narrowed because of a hot pustule which has come, then it is not necessary to work it, but rather things moist and fatty must be administered; and administer plasters, and sieges in soft and moist water. 
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on its side, and you can put it straight, so administer what we have said in a living child; and if one has no power, so the limb will be treated in parts, and leave nothing of the secondary.  
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if it is administered to those that we have said about abscesses which come in the marshes; and if bleeding occurs, then be put in vinegar restraining it, and administer other treatments.  
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly one child had been dead, then conceived another on top of it, and refused death to the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time there came an abscess in the belly, and it swelled so much that it opened, and began to drain profusely.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I pondered for a long time, and could not suture the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and from it came a bone, and after some days another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly amazed, because this one whose belly has no bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I sewed the wound, and in the hand bones, as long as the woman was in a better state; and the woman lived for a long time thus, and it seemed to her a little bow of pain from there; and I have not recalled this chapter except because, when the masters find a strange thing, that they should know how to put help. 
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the bone back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here after comes the form of the presser, which we have in the books; and at two turns at two joints of the two limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more subtle in the restrictor, and it should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the tube should be large, and the margins of the trees should be long, one palm and a half; and between the two limbs there should be two adjustments of this same tube, which are fastened in one and the other, of half a palm long or an inch more; and these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the mortise to open when one turns the two horns. 
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, similar in appearance more subtle and lighter, is made of ebony wood or boxwood, according to the appearance of the pliers; and have as II jaws II adjustments, as you see, an arm's length long, and II inches wide; and when you see open the mare with all the instrument, so make the woman sit on the bed, her feet hanging and her legs open, then put the II adjustments together in the mare, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs; then operate your hand on the whole instrument, as you have done with the pliers equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the mare, until the girl does what she wants. 
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument are all mounted, and are multiplied their likenesses; and when the viewer has seen them appeared, so much is more haste the work, and higher to men for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If it does not despise the instrument that you do not have it appeared, because their necessities is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is retained in childbirth, it is necessary that you command the woman to retain her arm, and then make her sneeze with condiments, and restrain her hands to her mouth and nose; and if she leaps for this, well is. 
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If this is not done, take a pot and make it porous or covered, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the fistula in it, such as calamine, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia leaf, and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, whether boiled or steeped in water on the fire; then place a strap or covering over the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the fistula, and leave it there until the vapors come from inside the fistula; then make it sneeze, as we have said. 
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second time he sneezes quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this cure, and there is no force, command the midwife to moisten her left hand in sesame oil or in an ointment of hellebore, and then put it into the vagina, and seek the second one; and when she has found it, seize it and extend it gently, so that the fetus does not fall out during the extraction; but you must move it lightly from side to side, and then pull; so it will come and be detached. 
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the marsh is too narrow, we have said the cure of sneezing, and fumigation of herbs; and if it is not from all that we have said, then guard that you do not use milk; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the marsh, you tie it to the hip of the woman, then clisterize with ointment tetrafarmaçon; if it will bear and return, and come forth; but nevertheless, when it bears so there comes bad odor to the stomach and head, and pales the patient. 
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore, it is necessary fumigations suitable for this: none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument for fumigating the woman at the time of childbirth is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is to be seen like a dog, and one puts the head subtle in the nature, and the shoulders wide above the fire; and let the fumigation be on the coals, and the soot until it is burned, and begin another. 
de percier lou fondement	to examine the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, but it is stopped with a subtle syfac: so it behooves the midwife to pierce that syfac at its right place, and do not pierce it with a sharp spatula, and guard the opening so she does not touch it; then put on a fleece moistened in wine and oil, then the cure of ointment until it is healed. 
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it does not return, then place upon it a piece of plank and leave it for many days, and remove it when the child wants to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And at times this stoppage comes from a scab of a wound or an abscess; so it is necessary to cover that scab; if cured, as we have said of the cautery of lead.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistules which come from under the foundation are nodules, and greater than those coming from near the foundation outside, or in the space of the two parts, if there is one fistula or several; and when that nodule is old, it works, and still moisture wakes white or subtle boils, and sometimes these fistulas pierce; and they are known by those who have them or discharge or wind when the patient makes a discharge, and perhaps in jumping some towards. 
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if fistulas that pierce to the bladder, and to half of the penis; and reach to the junction of the hip, and to the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula passing to the base, and not passing; and it is that you put your finger or base, and insert a fine needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no twisting. 
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is tortuosity, put in a tent of fine lead, or horsehair, until you feel the tent or hair at your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no emission from the outlet nor windiness nor liquid, as we have said: know that it does not pierce; so hurry to cure.  
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced to the bladder or to the urinary passage, if it leaks urine, and cannot be closed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced up to the joint of the hip, then the tendon coming to the place; if there is no tortuosity and the invention of pain around, then it is that there is a bow in it, and there is no medicine nor treatment by ointment; and in these fistulas piercing there is no cure except labor, and vanity of fools who intervene.  
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is neither too young nor too old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have proven, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and you raise the legs up to his hips, and have his hips inclined to his belly; then put a tent of iron, or of lead if there is tortuosity, as long as you know where the tent comes.  
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it near the foundation, then you should put your index finger there, feeling when he touches it; and be discovered or feel between your finger the syfac or the flesh, then you know that it is pierced; if one does not work on it one cannot heal it. 
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is said that one can heal some very well, but this happens rarely; and the aid one makes is thus: if one has heated the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula as has been said before, and it puts all hot into the fistula until it reaches the foundation; and do this II times or III, until you know that these burnt threads are burned, which are resembling an eye's feather; and then cure with moist tents in butter, until those threads have come out, then cure with oil ointment joining flesh and soldering. 
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healthy, it is well. 
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this is the case, it cannot be healed otherwise; and if it pulls inward, and does not reach to the point that is the base, and between your two tendons and the pull there is a thick covering of flesh or silk, and you see the fistula at this covering down towards the heart; so cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push forward the pull, and then cauterize afterwards, until it reaches the head of the pull; and it will be delivered, the pull, and fall; then remove those threads that seem like an owl's feather, and nothing remains. 
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the skin pulls out, and goes between you and the work, cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery assembles II good things: that is to say, the burning of these joined bones, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture; then the cure of wet bandages in butter or in crushed herbs, as long as the wound lies open, and if the bones are burned in the wound; then cure the wound of sudden swellings by applying hard dough, and those medicines are dry. 
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes all the way down to the bottom and is separated from the body, you put your hand or foundation there and examine it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between it is the cloth or the syfac or chars, where it is near to piercing, if there is no other way except by faith and hope, by the administration of one of the three manners: or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can put tents and cure as before; and do not go too deep in that you do not cut the tenement that holds the foundation, and come the egestions by that sense will; then cure, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and the munde once it is cut from its foundation, or by tent or by other instrument pointed; then moundify that char fautree which is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to remain the fistula in the part outside the foundation: so will be a lighter thing for the patient. 
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this manner: and when you put the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side of the base next to the skin above, then take a tent perforated at the top according to this form. 
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And he puts one twisted thread into two, and puts the tent on all the thread in the fistula as long as it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the margin of the foundation within, then extract the thread of that which is pierced, as you place your foot or foundation; and treat the head of the thread, and assemble the two heads together, and restrain one to the other, and let it be for a day or two; and restrain it no times, until the threads cope those chars that are between two, and stick; then cure the wound until it is joined and healed. 
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, then make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if it is not too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not behoove to make by the lacing cover if too deeply embedded, and then cure it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spathulate spine from which one makes the fistula is very uneven on one side and trenches; and on the other side no, because one doesn't cut what one shouldn't cut, as you see here: 
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhages are according to II manners: or they are within the foundation, like a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in short, some blood, and there are one or more, and they are outside the foundation and at the head of the foundation; but those that are outside have little moisture, and in short, or a little bit of citrine water or a little blood, and they have the color of the body; and the cure of those who have them within the foundation, is that you order the patient to stretch himself to go into chambers, as long as the foundations are issued out, and the threads appear; if you hurry, and can hold them with pliers, or you hold it with your finger, then cut them at their roots; and if the tweezers cannot hold them for their moisture, then take them with the drapeil, or with cotton, or a piece of chamelot; and extract them to your thumbs, then cut them, and powder them with some hot powders that are in their place of cautery; or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter of cautery, then cure them from other cures until he is healed; and if the foundations cannot issue out, then clisterize the patient with a harsh and sharp clyster to wash what is in the foundation, so that it may issue openly; when the patient strains, and if the threads are outside the foundation, then the cure is light; and it is that you pick them up with your finger or with pliers, and cut them, then cure them as we have said, until he is healed, and that he fears the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you bring the stitch according to this manner: take I thread tort, and put it in a needle, and then draw the thread upward and make pierce the needle on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and so be of the wide; and tighten the thread form, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do thus of all the others, and leave one for correcting the superfluity of the blood; then put upon the foundation I drapelet moist in rose oil or in cerote, and put upon the foundation, and command to the patient that he rests; and then leave him as long as it is necessary, and when they will be dry, so cure with ointment and other cures, until it is healed. 
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Dryness of the bowels or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times dryness of the bowels occurs in the intestine, and by constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is not effective.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you scrape at the point of a spatula or with your fingernail the bark above, which does not let it become moist; then treat it until it heals as much as is needed; and if it cannot heal, restart scraping more strongly than before, until it heals well, and is scraped off; then treat it until it is healed. 
dou fremit	Of trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formic is a small appearance false before the body, and goes much in harming; and sometimes she finds it cold, and feels it one also like dead of trembling, and comes into all the body, and more to the hands than other parts. 
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a cane of an owl's feather, or a vulture's feather very strong, and put that cane on the furrow, until the purple circles stain the furrow all around; then turn your hand to all the cane until you cut all around the furrow, and put it in apart, and scrape the furrow from its roots. 
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, so do this of a dog of iron or steel according to this form, and be subtle below and trailing above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, for the two to hold, and move pressed And if you see, so cauterize the frenulum, as it is before or in the chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the clister
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	At no time is made a clister of silver or wood, or iron melted or woven; and at no time is made of these instruments small and large, according to those to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those therefore who are administered in the care of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clyster small and large if it is above wide, or the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And there is a severance where the belly is tied, as you see, and the head is pierced inside; and on one side it has II holes, and on the other I; and the belly is where one puts medicines in a bladder of beast or parchment, and is pierced all around with small holes, and there is between each hole I space, then put in these holes I strong thread of thread cut twisted in X or in which around, and assemble the belly as if it were a kid; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front of a strong thread, then give an enema; and this is the form of the circle. 
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the chief with clyster of oil or of egg yolk, or something similar, then insert it gently; then the minister presses the ministers with his two hands together, until he is completely wet, then remove the clyster, and raise the patient's legs to the side, and if the medicine wants to flow out, let it flow as much as possible; and if he sleeps all night, then there is greater aid. 
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you enema the patient with illness of stomach pain, and the medicine works quickly, then repeat it until he is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the foundation or abscess, so is the clyster as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle clyster on which the skin is restrained:  
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in the division the cure of wounds; now we will tell you the cures of hands and medicine, according to accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by blows of stone, and sword cuts and knives, or spear or staff or arrow, or similar things; which are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or head, or back, or belly, or liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with wounds of the head simples, because the remembrance comes in this chapter.
