Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, if you take care that it is of kidney stone or similar things, and the skin is immediately torn and the wound is large, and you doubt heavily abscess heat: then I make it healthy from the cephalic itself, even if it comes little blood from the wound, and let the bloodletting be on the contrary of the diseased part; and avoid the patient repletion of wine and heavy meats. 
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to bleed, let his meat be reduced, and let him drink no wine, nor eat any meat; and put on the wound, if an abscess comes there, moistened cotton in rose oil only, or in styptic wine; and if there is no abscess hot, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, powder, which I will say a little later; and if it has been moved by the air, put on some ointment, until it is healed. 
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together with tents, then assemble them with stitches, as I will say for belly wounds, of stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone, and is hanging, and only holds on by a bit, then cut it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat large meats, such as beef and wheat cooked, also poultry, and similar things. 
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find a rotting skin, and it does not reach the bone, so cut all the rot away, and throw it out, then cure; and if it has an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped without cutting, and it cannot be stopped by medicine, then sever the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.  
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and it is that you put in this powder which binds as soon as the wound has closed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and grind the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and hold it firmly, until it dries well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it well, and leave it untied, if it does not swell; for one removes the medicine only when it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at no time is this made with only quicklime when one has neither incense nor dragon’s blood, but that the fire has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire has cauterized the wound, even in its state, do not put on this powder; but put some digested ointments, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it softens; then cure other cures until it is healed.  
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, so extract it with fine pincers; and I will tell you here afterward the fractures of the head.  
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	This wound comes from the neck and it is simple, if there is no difference between this one and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there is no other thing to leave the cure, and do not put anything restraining, because it harms the nerves and makes them retract; and do not put on the wound anything cold, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of it is with the brain, which is the highest member; but be the medicine warm, such as hazel washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and boiled water also in sweet water, and other stones of mine according to this manner, and moist ointments.  
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then stitch it and tie it with bandages, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and she is covered and full of pus, then pierce or lower them; and if the artery is cut, and blood flows, then stop it, and bind it, and cauterize as necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the conduction is guarded, so that the flesh goes, then sew the heart on the chain of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural form; and then bind it firmly, and leave it for some days, then cure with ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then remove it; and if there are pieces of bone, treat them externally as much as you can, and those that you cannot have, then leave them until the wound decays, and become free and aligned its issue; and if the wound is fresh, put powder on the powder that I have said. 
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and it has a fistula, treat it as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or a sword, and the wound is deep, see if from the wound there are puffs of wind as the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh in all its blood, do not put anything on it at first hour, nor bind it tightly for fear that the blood does not drain deeply and returns to the heart, and harms the patient; but put attractive ointment on it, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on his wound for 3 days, or 4, or more; so that there comes no spasm, nor bad tremor of the heart nor constraint of the breath; and when you see the good dispositions, know that the wound is saved.   
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Therefore treat with tents and other treatments, until it is healed; and if it cannot heal and works, then recognize that there is a fistula; then treat the fistula as one should.  
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or worse, or on the back, then the cure of that which is in front; if it is large, stitch it; and if it is small, with powder; and if it is embedded in bone, and has struck pieces, then care for the wound, and pull out the fragments if they are loose; and if they are not loose, then let the wound rot, so that it will lighten the extractions; and for other wounds on other limbs is judgment as we have said.  
dou derrompement dou ventre	Of the displacement of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is large and medium and small; from a great wound, sometimes the intestine, or the nerve of the intestines comes out, because of which there is intrusion of something else; and the suture is more difficult, and sometimes it is worse than the small wound that the large one, because for this reason one puts the intestines back in with more care, unless they put them back quickly into hot; because the intestine inflates as soon as they feel cold, so they enter in more carefully, and for this reason the medium wound is worse for this reason, for which reason one brings the intestine back to its place that others II And know that the rupture of the belly is according to IV manners: the II sutures common happen in the suture of the belly, and the suture of other wounds of the body and II other sutures are proper common to other wounds; and anyway they are more proper with the suture of the belly, and I will say one by one and declare. 
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine is protruding, and it is necessary to close it, this is done in one of two ways: or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen from the cold. 
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: soak a sponge or a soft cloth in hot water only, or you cook in hot water with squill and cypress and spice, and raise the intestine until the swelling is removed; and sometimes do this restraining, and move it that it alone be untied to deflate.  
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or ale and malves be cooked, because by this is aligned the entrance to a little thing; and if it cannot enter, make a hole in the wound with the instrument with which one copes hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to move that the tail, that no one should cut it unless there is great necessity; and this is the instrument for fending: so cut inside into the curve and outside not, and see here the form. 
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine has fallen out, put it back in place according to its natural form, if you are able, because this helps healing. 
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the part below the belly, then you should make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part below the belly, then put the head and the hips higher than the parts below, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, then put your attention to that the wounded part be higher than the other; and thus you should administer what I say in large and medium wounds.  
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	Small wounds put that which appears to you, then hold between your hands the minister pitiful who holds all the rupture in his hand, and assemble the lips; and this is the common manner of stitching, and is that you prick a needle or more, according to the quantity of the breadth of the wound, then leave from the chief of the wound one span of space, and there put a needle where it has good strong thread; and pierce the two heads of the skin with the two heads of the siphac, which is under the skin within, as long as you make it pierce from that part, and assemble the two chiefs of the siphac together; then the strain of a double thread around the needle of two parts, then assemble the two heads of the wound again, and then leave one span of space, and there put another needle; then the tie of the thread like as you have done the first needle, and do not cease to do so according to what you have need of needles, until the whole wound is restrained; and let the needles be medium, between subtle and thick, for the subtle needles cut all the flesh, and the too thick ones cannot well enter: therefore it behoves that they be medium; and it behoves not to put the needles too far out of the flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound before the suture; and then cut the heads of the needles, so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and there put tents or bandages at the heads of the needles for the muse to hold, and leave them until the wound is sutured; and this manner of stitching with needles is more convenient in small wounds, for there suffices one needle or two for the second stitch, which is common, and is that you assemble the two heads of the skin and the two heads of the siphac together on a needle where it has good medium thread; and when you have pierced these heads all together, then move the needle to the part where you have commenced, in the manner in which one sews the clothes; and put space between each stitch the thickness of a finger span; this suture is used by men, and I sewed a wound on a man's belly, who was wounded with a knife, and the wound was more than a palm wide, and it was intestines well two palms wide, and the wound was in the middle of the belly. 
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back his intestine after it had been out for 24 hours, and the wound closed up for 15 days, and I treated him, and he was cured.  
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the wise men had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not heal him with ointment, because I was in that place where one could find none, nor any medicine; and I put upon the wound cotton old II times a day, and washed it with honey water until it was healed. 
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the II proper ways of stitching: take the needle, and put it from the outside part to the inside; when it has pierced the core straight on straight, lay the point down on the skin or where you have put the needle, and make it pierce from the other side, from the inside to the outside; and the understanding of this stitch is that you stitch as the furrier does furs, and that you leave one side of the skin once, and take it back another, until the stitching is all complete. 
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of stitching, which the Galicians say properly, is like any font, which brings together the two parts naturally, and apply one end to the other end, in this manner: pierce a needle or end of mirach near, and make it pass through that place alone, and leave the two ends of the syfac; then turn the needle, and make it pass from the outside part to the inside, at the two ends of the syfac; then make it pass through one and the other, from the outside part to the inside, in two other ends of mirach that are on the other side; and this is the most common manner of stitching. 
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galians says this word, and no one testifies to it, one must sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each; and one must push one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew belts; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the suture is more grievous than the others of the belly. 
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of the other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, just as soon as the artery has been moved, then put back the intestine, and the gut; then put on powder enjanrant char, and if the artery has been moved, then put on any ointment that is present, until the wound bows; and stitch the thread, and be joined the sifac, and the mirach; then cure the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then put on, as soon as it begins to get bowed, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.  
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	Because you do not have need of other medicine in many dispositions as long as the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not make communion with the principal members, it is necessary that you moisten the linen lightly in oil of tempered heat, or in rose oil, and put it around the angles, and under the buttocks; and if it feels pain or putrefaction in bowls, which happens many times, so the clysters of black wine help, and even if the putrefaction comes to the intestine; and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small. 
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is pierced, and this is because of the delicacy of the veins that are in it, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves. 
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the thread jumps from the wound, put it back in as well as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become black or dark, then you must tie the place that is black, so that bleeding does not come from there, because there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ligature, and put the two heads hanging from the part below the wound up to outside in order to align the extraction when the thread falls and the wound bows.  
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is pierced, and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, because I saw that one man was struck in his belly by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and became a fistula, and through it there was discharge and flatulence; I put treatment according to what I could, and did not stop working until he was healed, and the edges were soldered.  
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sutured, I doubted that the patient was ill in his belly; and there was no harm, but he remained in better dispositions, and ate and drank; and some experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied in this manner: take two reeds with large heads, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the reed has covered the mouth, put it on the two lips so that it strains its mouth upwards; and then cut off the head, and it stays so that it cannot untie, then put another reed afterwards in the same manner as before, until the wound is entirely captured; and stitch the wound. 
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the head is set in the intestine, and no nuisance comes to the patient, one can tie the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of a beast, in this manner: take the head of this intestinal thread that be well cleaned, and then tie it to the head of this linen thread twisted thin, then put the thread in the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it back into the rupture; and this manner of stitching of threads is not worse than according to the way of fiance and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the main intestines, there is nothing but subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it opens, is universally called “fistula,” and even when it is healed and closed inward.  
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the truth knotted false and white, where one does not feel pain, and it is also shaped like the feather of a bird; and sometimes clear bowe, and other times thick; sometimes small, and other times enough; and I have spoken about it in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is nothing but by one of the IX causes: that is to say, by the little blood or body; or for its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the lips, which does not allow flesh to be born; or there is too much bowe; or the layers are rotten, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because corruption is a manner of pestilence; or because the property in the region is late digestion, and slow healing, and swollen by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and cures of medicines in the division. 
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Therefore it is necessary that I make you know the cure of a fistula which is done by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and to the arteries, and to the nerves, or to the liver, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and so on that it comes to the propriety of the principal member, and to similar ones. 
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are of this manner are of grievous healing, and there is only labor, and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place that I have said, and you have faith in the cure, and you want to know it, then take a tent of iron or of fer, if the fistula is straight, so much. And if the fistula is crooked, so wrap it with a subtle tent of lead, because lead bends itself around the tortuosity; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well wrap it with tents, so clistetize it by one of the openings, because the moisture comes from one opening to another, and it cleanses; then wrap it sagely according to your power, that you know if there is bone or nerve, and is healed in depth, and ask the patient well about the pain that he feels when pressing with your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you will truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from the joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, so cut according to what I have told you, and remove the foul matter and corrupt matter that are inside; then cure until it is healed, and if the fistula is well deep and right, then it is necessary that you cut in depth, as much as you can, then put moistened tents in a medicine of vinegar, and put them to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that is remaining at the bottom; then put ointments of healthy flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by these, so cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, so cut it. 
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerves or principal members do not trouble you as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered and there is corruption and blackness, then cleanse it as long as the corruption is entirely removed, then cure the flesh with things that come after until it is healed; and if it is not healed and returns like before, know that you have not gone as far as the bottom: uncover and search as long as you are at the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore it in its place; and if it is so healed, it is good.  
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this is not the case, know that corruption is too far along, that you cannot come to it; if there is nothing else but to leave it to nature; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can extract it with pliers, then extract it with a suitable instrument for this, and if there are many bones, then treat them all, do not leave even one; and if the moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, then cut both the moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones. 
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, put on the wound something preventing rot, and leave until the flesh is rotten around the bones, then they will have more easily the bones; and if it is a large bone, such as of leg or thigh, so let it be only the corruption as long as the black is entirely removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a great part of the corruption, and comes to the marrow of the bone; so it should be sewn and covered until the corruption, and then cure it until it is joined; and I will tell you of a fistula which happened to a man in his leg, so that you take example from it and help in your work. 
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man about XXX years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, until the materials came to the leg, and it swelled with a large abscess, and there was no external cause to open; but the surgeons by their folly operated so much that the abscess opened, and they corroded much matter, and it became a fistula, and there came many openings that all secreted moist from the body; and many surgeons treated it for about II years, and there was no wise man in the art of hands, until I was called to him, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which he was treated, and what ran through the openings with great pus; and the young man's skin became red, and had a yellow color. 
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I covered a tent over one of these pits, and then I searched all the pits, and found that some came opposite each other from all parts of the leg. 
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened therefore, and scraped in one of the openings until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption came up to the inner bone; I saw what appeared to me of the rotten bone, and thought that there was no other corruption except that which I had removed; and I began to restore the wound with healing medicines for a long time, and could not join it; and then I began again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, and I saw it, and then removed it, and decided to solder the place; but I could not more than I scraped around an arm's length of the bone, and the trail was throughout its whole thickness, then I restored it with medicines; and it became healthy and joined quickly, and it did not need to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had of him. 
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Because for the evacuation of blood often, but it was healed entirely, and in place of the bone grew a hard cartilage, and he was of good disposition and did not have any harm or opposite at all, neither in going nor coming.  
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, it should be treated this way: take a linen cloth, and bind it to the head of the bone that opens, and order someone who will extend it upward; and put another linen cloth thicker than the first linen, and tie it above the skin that is over the bone, and extend the head, so that you draw the corrupted skin down, and uncover the skin in the place where you want to be, so that the bone does not bleach the skin; and put a stick or a board under the bone so that the corrupted skin can be covered; and it should be treated as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and it should be treated again. 
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open well, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover all the flesh; then put a hot coal underneath, and then move it from one side to the other of the corruption, and let the ligature be as long as the extent of the corruption; and if the corruption is at the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and move the bone or where it contains from the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is nothing else that needs to be done but to cut; and if the corruption is in the finger of the hand, or in the finger of the foot, then this thing is very strong, but nonetheless, it is necessary that you examine this corrosion, how it opens for you; and purify it in all ways that you can, but that the vein or nerve does not hinder you; and know that the instruments to cut these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of them, and their thickness and their thinness, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness; and for this reason it is necessary to prepare for each kind of work its instrument; and know that the work will show you the instrument that you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of illnesses; so consider the instrument which you need according to what it befits.  
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joint can be affected either from within or from without; and when you have treated the corrosion with medicine, and it does not benefit, then it is necessary to cover that limb up to the place where the corrosion comes from so that the patient escapes by this from death, or from the malice which is greater, of the fault of the limb; and the signs are that the limb becomes black, so that it seems as though it has been burned by fire, and after the blackness it proceeds, then the corrosion of the limb goes from limb to limb, and takes over the whole body; therefore hasten to cover it, and if it is due to the puncture of some venomous beasts, such as a scorpion of the sea and a viper and similar ones, if the corrosion is at the head of the thigh, then cover it, and do not give him any space to come up to the hand.  
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, cut at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no other treatment except the quantity of its virtue; and thus do all when the corrosion comes or foot: if it comes on the first joint, cut after the other joint; and if it comes on the foot, cut the whole foot; and if it goes up the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other means than to leave the patient to die; and the manner of cutting or sewing the limb is that you bind it above and below, and stretch one minister on one of the ties down, and another minister on the other tie up, and you loosen the flesh which is between the two ties a spatula wide, so that the bone be uncovered; then cut or sew, and put on each side the bandage of linen, so that the sewing does not touch the healthy place, and comes to the patient another lesion and abscess. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you work, cauterize the place carefully, or put on some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the affected limb with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his foot: he had a blackness that seemed burned by fire, and this corrosion first came in his heel, until it covered the whole foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hurried to cover his foot, and it was healed; and long after this, the corrosion returned in his hand, and he came to me, and I put on some corrective things after the purification of the body, and could not stop the corrosion; and he begged that I should amputate his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of correcting the matter; and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would die, because the virtue of the man was weak; and he despaired of all, and returned to his land, and hurried to cover his hand, and it was healed; and I have recounted this story only for this reason, so that one can do otherwise, if one has need. 
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess comes in a fleshy place, and stays for so long that it makes a large gathering of pus; and then it bursts and pierces, and from the pus the skin leaps up, like vessels; and the skin which is above is as subtle as delicate veils, and does not go to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a sickness is called "a boil", and is not called "a fistula"; but if it is so long that it comes to the bone or penetrates it, then it is called "a fistula"; and the skin of it is that you cut that skin all around, even when it is subtle, like delicate veils; and it does not get worse for its corruption. 
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have faith that the skin is hardened, and the corruption is not in full progress, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with this enema: see if the breast is large, and the bow which is in it is of a foul odor, then administer an enema of Egyptian medicine which is made thus: take equal parts of honey, oil, and litharge, and put them into a vessel over the fire until the medicine becomes red, and as thick as honey; and then take of this according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and enema the breast, and restrain the anus; and leave the medicine inside for two hours, then withdraw it by squeezing; do this many times until the breast is disinfected, and the odor is removed; and sometimes administer an enema of water from ashes when this medicine is not present, and that you take ashes from vine wood, and pour water on top, then filter it, and enema with it, until you know that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot endure either the Egyptian medicine nor the water from ashes, then enema with water and honey or a little ground litharge; or enema them with honey and mellow wine so that the honey has the property of purifying and washing, and the wine dries the flesh; and when you have done this, and you are convinced that the breast is well cleansed, then administer an enema of that which causes flesh to grow in it, and that you take diaphinit plaster, and mix it with rose oil and wine; or enema them with other medicines and ointments, about whose properties I have already spoken or treated of ointments; and if the opening of the breast is small, and the tube of the enema cannot enter, then enlarge a bit with iron, and put inside a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basil ointment, until it is enlarged; and if the wound is too wide, then stitch and leave only the space where the enema can enter, and if the opening that emits foul odor is on top, then place the cup or lower part where it is.  
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bow is set in place, there shall not be any fat left in it; and if you cannot cover the chest underneath as well as you want, then arrange it in such a manner that the bow goes to the lowest point where it is, for when the bow is set in place, there shall not be any fat left in it, and if you cannot cover the chest underneath as well as you want, then arrange it in such a manner that the bow goes gently downwards, and do not leave anything of the bow; and take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and stay upon the linen cloth that covers the whole wound; then cut as forces near the opening of the chest, slightly wider than the first, then place ointment under the other cloth according to the quantity of the opening, and place it on the opening of the wound to align the bow, and do not remove the large cloth except after many days once; and the one that is on the opening of the chest, often removed to remove the bow, and know what runs from the bow, whether it is poison or a little or enough, digested, or indigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or no, and if there is an abscess or not, and when the medicine has spread in such a manner and you see the nature that leaps upon the opening of the wound, then know that the chests are healing already, and approaching health; and then untie it in the morning, or the third day, and when you untie the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment. 
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast remains bowed undigested after many days, know that the breast does not heal well.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons come after a long time, if it does not trouble your health, for the cure is approaching.  
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	Because there are men whose healing of flesh in their wounds is slow, and some who do the opposite; and if a boil arises indigestible from the chest after many days, know that the breasts do not close well; and if the breasts take long to heal and are distant, then apply drying medicines moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as diaphinit ointment, because there is much vitriol in it, and this is the last medicine; take diaphinit ointment, and make it with rose oil, and the aroa of old wine equal in substance; then confit it and use it; and these same things are made with honey cooked more than once when diaphinit ointment is not present, or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them, and powder them on the honey when it is over the fire; and then glue I draped, and place it on the breast, and no times administer a long aristolochia, and roots of lis celeste, which is also like flour of vicis and centaury; and use simple or composed: grind them, and make them powder, and put them on the honey that I have said, and use; and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this cure, then know that the corruption is deep-seated, and makes impressions in the bone, or in hard members, or in limbs; so the cure of the fistule, as we have said before. 
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the angle
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises under the nail of the hand, or the foot, or perhaps in other parts; and when it becomes inflamed and one does not take care of it, then it comes to a suppurating abscess, and runs and eats away the flesh until it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps all of it; and the corrosion comes to the bone, so that there is painful pus, and the limb becomes swollen, and the color is foul. 
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you cut to it, iron all the superfluity which is remaining of the ulcer, then cauterize the wound afterward.  
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses on the flesh, and it begins to prick, and the blue, then you must put the root under the nail that point the flesh, and push it up, and cut that flesh subtly and lightly, and put on the remaining flesh medicines burning and corrosive to remove everything; then cure with ointments until it is healed. 
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut it and treat it, because as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see it about to corrupt, then cut it in I before us as it was said, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is broken, and pushed, and it feels great pain, then you must first heal it; then cut the angle of the spatula sharp by cutting across above, and ward that the cut does not come to the flesh which is below the angle, because the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, then put something on top that soothes.  
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain from the hand is relieved
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints which are born in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is some where it has bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and none of these are born at the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of us in the thumbs. 
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in any nout of the hip does not move, and he who is born at the joint of the hip, perhaps moves; the size of the one who is fleshy is so light, in this manner: cut it at its root with a wide spatula. 
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born in the root of the joint, that is grievous to cure; so hold you to cut.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or must at the rear end, it is necessary that you cut first the flesh round to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable place for him, then treat it until it is healed. 
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The solderings that come to the two assemblies come from birth, or from the welding of a wound, or from the burning of fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If it is necessary that you cut the suture so that the parts repair according to their natural forms; then put between two tents or cloths moistened in rose oil, so that they do not join; or you put between two pieces of subtle plank, until the joints are joined, as it is necessary. 
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the joint comes to any of its two with the palm, then strike that solder as it is fitting.
des vils	of villages 
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large and swollen with melancholy superfluities, which come in more members of the body; and there is more often in legs of those who walk and work and carry, than others.  
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore it is necessary that you administer to him once expurgation of honey, and then the ointment of the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is in two ways: one is to cut and draw out the black blood; and the other manner is that you open a vein and treat it thoroughly.  
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The thigh is treated in this manner: first raise the leg of warm water very strongly until the hard vein becomes softened, then hold the leg of the patient from above the hip to below the knee; then cut a vein in one place, or another, or third place, with a wide incision, then elevate and squeeze out the black blood from one end to the other, as much as the strength of the patient can endure; then apply the ligature, and order him to stay on meat diet until it is black; and begin the evacuation and the bloodletting when the veins are full, and hurt the patient.   
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The raising of the leg is done in this manner: take the leg of the patient, if there are many hairs, then put it in a bath, and raise the leg in hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell; and if you have no bath, then heat it by the fire, and then cut above the vein from the top of the knee to the foot, or in the part below the ankle; then open the skin with a knife, and scrape the vein on each side, until it appears when one feels it; and it is seen red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord; then put the blade under, until it is raised from the skin, and then place it on the knife lightly, then cut it in another place above three fingers; then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears, then raise it to the point, as you have done, and place it on another knife, as you did first; then cut another piece, or more if you need it, then raise it, and cut at the top of the foot, then pull and raise it up to the second cut; then extract from cut to cut, until it is all brought out, then cut; and if you cannot pull and raise it, put a needle in the whole strong thread double, and tie it and pull it, and put it under the point, and turn your hand on one side and the other, until it comes out; and be careful that it does not break, because if it breaks, it cannot be pulled or raised, and it causes discomfort to the patient; and when you have treated it all, put a piece of wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the place of the wound; and dress it until it is healed. 
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it twisted, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before. 
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of the iron with which one cuts the vein is curved, and it does not cut, so that it only cuts the vein; and is of thick curvature, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein, but be thick as we have said, and here is the form: 
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein 
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in legs, in hot parts where there do not grow herbs or trees, and in land that has no moisture; and by chance it can be born elsewhere than in legs, and this happens because of the rot that comes under the skin, as it comes from within the body serpents and worms, trapped between skin and flesh. 
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that it comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then it changes its places, and begins the vein to issue out, as much as a root of a plant.
