Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the shoulder head opens, it behoves you to wrap around a piece of plank from one and a half to two inches, and knot it, and leave the plank on the leg, and every time that there is point in the fire, wrap around the plank, and tie it; and if it is too long, cut off a part, and wrap the remaining portion, and do not cut it at its root, until it is completely out; for if you cut it, it enters into the flesh, and brings forth abscesses and putrefaction there, and bad sickness; for this reason it behoves that it be treated bit by bit up to the head, and nothing remains in the body; and sometimes this vein when it is treated of V palms long, or X, and one son came to me once, to whom it was X palms long, and when you cut it, it brings out the root or spur, and pierce it to the bottom, so that all comes out; and empty the matter that is inside, and administer medicines there to prevent putrefaction any day, then cure it like the abscesses. 
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes at this vein mains rains, and similarly when it opens in the joint of the foot, or the foot, and there comes much of the hurt, and from which it jumps rains; cure then as we have said before.  
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that are born between skin and flesh 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land "ox disease," because it happens many times to oxen, and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body going up and down, and one feels it well at the alarm of limb to limb, as long as it goes through the skin where it goes, and jumps further; and it is caused by rot of some humors, such as worms and serpents and embers and ascarides in the belly; and one doubts its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it climbs to the head, and it comes to the eye, perhaps it enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times. 
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see him cure and treat, one can only flee when he goes: so it is necessary that you bind the place above and below with a strong rope tightly, then cut above and treat the fur, and if the worm goes deep into the flesh, and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm that it does is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said; and if you see him coming or chief near the eye, then restrain below him the eyebrow forming, then cut above, and treat the fur; and it is necessary to use the patient of purification of body of medicines solutives for the bad humors porries, and avoid eating rotten meat. 
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in some limbs, and then moves from limb to limb; and I have seen what I tell you.  
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and a little after, I saw it rise like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, as if alive silver when it leaves one place for another; the pain departed from that place, and went into the shoulder, and then a little after corrupted throughout the whole body, until she came to the other arm; then she told me that she returned towards the body again, as I saw her. 
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I never wished this illness in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had wanted many to be moved from their pain to another place, but I did not want it, as I saw it in the woman; and I thought that this was because the woman had a dry body, and the veins exposed, and for that reason appeared that constraint of windiness; and they do not appear according to this reason those who are delicious, and who have moist bodies and covered veins.  
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to cure this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have said, then lie above and below gently, and then cut above until the windiness is constrained to its place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then cure with those who loosen the windiness, such as fetid pills, and pills of serapin, and similar others.  
des saiettes	of arrows 
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The variety of them is that there are some which have large points, and small, and hairy, and welded; and those which have II angles, and those which have tongues, and those where there are pieces; and the one that falls in any member it falls according to II manners: or in a principal member such as brain, heart, liver, lung, reins, intestine, bladder, and similar members.  
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When she falls then in any place of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you afterwards, appear to you: it is necessary that you desist from the extraction of this arrow, because death comes afterwards in many dispositions; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not yet deeply embedded, then treat, and cure the wound. 
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow strikes it and pierces the bone, and jumps the sifac which is above the brain, is when there is scotomy and swelling and turning and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of phlegm; and perhaps without a discharge from the nostrils, or the ears; and perhaps loses speech and voice; and jumps from the wound moisture white resembling to poultices, and jumps also as burning of flesh; and if this sign appears to you, then hold yourself back from the cure, and treat the arrow if it is not yet in. 
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the seventh when it falls or heart, are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were tied in something hard, not empty; and by chance the seventh moves as the poultice, and in short black blood, and comes coldness and sweat cold, and fainting: know then without doubt that death is present. 
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the seventh that does not move is that without plain foam jumping from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and gasps loudly and shivers with cold.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the hip, it is near the ribs; and it gives great pain and much sorrow and sighing; and they move all the members of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls into the stomach, by chance it jumps from the wound some thing of undigested flesh.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly, and jumps a point of fiber through the intestine root, there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes forth, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, like the face and neck and throat and shoulder and arm and spine of the back and thigh and hip and legs, and the seeming member, are safe according to more dispostitions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for that you do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man with an arrow that shot into the root of his nose: I touched it, and pulled it out from the other side under the fat of the ear, and it was healed without feeling at all.  
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And treat with an arrow that it fell into the fat of the eye below the paper below, and the arrow was replaced, and could not be reached except the tip towards the shaft, and the arrow was large as a Turkish bow, to all its iron light without ears; the player was unharmed, and no bad accidents befell him.  
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And treated an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabian with ears: I removed the barbs, and carefully extracted it as much as I could, and the Christian became healthy. 
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And treated an arrow to the man, who it was in his chest or belly, and thought he would die; and then that he had passed XXX days, he did not change his condition; I cut on the arrow, and cauterized it, and pulled it out, and there was no bad accident. 
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man who has an arrow in his back or shoulder, and the wound is sewed up; and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change its natural position, nor finds nuisance in any of his natural works. 
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see I another man, to whom a bolt fell in his face, and the wound was closed; and he remained thus suffering great pain; and many other similar things. 
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And treated an arrow in the man of the princes the king, that it was stuck in his groin, and was a little leaning to the right side; and the arrow was all lodged, I was called to the cure after it was stuck for three days.  
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If found the wound very tight.  
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I felt it with a whole subtle tent, and did not feel it at all; and he felt pricking and pain below his right ear. 
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the plaster on his hand for several days, and sutured the wound directly, and left the patient like that for a long time, until he felt the arrowhead one day inside his flesh; and he told me this. 
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put on the wound medicine corrosive by hand for several days, until it was open, and I touched it, and felt the head of the arrow which hardened in place; then I adjusted it into the opening of the wound with that same corrosive medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me; and it stayed well for four months, and then widened so much that I put the pliers on it, and the mine on one side and the other, and it could not go out; therefore I did not stop refining and devising instruments in ways, until I took one day the pliers well made, according to those which its form will come at the end of this chapter, until I extracted it, and restored the wound. 
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the healers judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I restored it then, and was joined the wound, and was healed the patient entirely. 
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your care on those which I do not say, because the books cannot comprehend everything; but the wise masters compare on well little thing, and on those which are present and lacking, find new work, and new instruments, at the descent of strange things which happen in this art. 
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows are not found in the limbs where they are lodged except according to two manners: either by the place where they enter, or by another part; and that which is found by the place where it enters, it is an arrow entering into the flesh, and that which is none of these times. 
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump now, let it be so until the child is carried around, and it be relieved at the exit; and also if it is fixed in the bone, and it cannot exit, let it be left thus for several days, and move it each day; and then if it jumps, and if it does not jump, then pierce around to all the forest fine, until the surroundings are enlarged, and then treat it. 
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head, and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient: do not remove it, but leave it there until it is equal after several days, because if the arrow comes as far as the syphysis, it is death. 
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone and does not come to the surface and the patient remains for some days without bad accident, then the engine of the milk. 
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very stuck like this and cannot be pulled out further, then administer turpentine as I have told you; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is put back in its place in the body, if one cannot see it, then search for it with all your strength; and if you feel it, then treat it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones or nerves or vein, then widen as much as the wound is large; and treat the arrow if you can, and if it has ears to which it is attached, then remove the flesh that is stuck on the two parts as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, as much as you can draw it out; and be careful that you do not break the arrow, that you will draw it out more violently. 
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, then lay him down until his limbs are relaxed, then treat him, for the extraction is easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bloodletting makes you contrary, then administer what we have said of the cure in its chapter; and guard against incision of the nerve and vein, and put everything as well as you can draw out the arrow without peril, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form that it was when the arrow fell into him, for this is the greatest help that there be, and if you cannot, then put it according to what the signs show you. 
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where one does not see anything of it, or the skin is swollen in place so that if one sees or feels it apparently: cut then on top, as long as the pliers can take it, and then extract it: if it jumped out now. 
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be pulled out, leave it still, and then begin the extraction again until it comes out; and if there is an arrow in it, push it with all force; and if the shaft has fallen, and you see to administer a pushing instrument, administer it as carefully so that the point of the arrow enters into the head of the instrument; and then push further, and if the arrow is stuck, push the instrument again with its point entering inwards, in order to facilitate the extraction. 
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is surrounded, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as it is necessary.  
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls or on the belly or on the bladder or on the ribs, and it is near, and you can cover above, if you cover it; and guard yourself from covering the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew the wound, if necessary is; and care for it until it is healed. 
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to treat arrows resembles that of an eye, and behold here the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the head of the spear is also like the feather of a bird, to pierce at the point of the arrow, as this is its shape. 
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of pliers to insert and to grasp is this.
des voinnes dou cors communes	Of veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Of the veins from which one is healed are XXXI, of this there are XVI at the head; that is to say: II battens which are after the ears, which are called the two "herbech"; and the II arteries which are in the II temples apparent; and II veins that are in the II tear ducts of the II eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the neck; and the II veins which are on the collarbone; and the II veins that are on the upper lips, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and II veins that are under the tongue. 
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins which are commonly opened in each arm: one is the cephalic and it is on the left side, and the common people call it “vein of the head”; and the middle one is called “fast,” and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilica, and the common people call it “vein of the heart”; and the basilica is on the right side, and the common people call it “vein of the belly”, and it is above the fossil, and it is the one that is opened, which opens clearly over the pouch. 
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saphenous vein is the one between the ring finger and the little finger, and it has two tributaries; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: the one is below the curve of the pocket of the left side, and the second saphenous which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein that is called "saphena", which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those. 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The blood of the veins that are after the ears so helps with old catarrhs and migraines; and the qualities of the vein, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a vise, until the two veins appear behind the ears in their places depending on the head: so aim your right, and where you feel the pulse below your right, seize it; then take the lancet, and put it below the vein to the bone, then lift your hand over the entire vein above, and cut through both skin and vein well two fingers deep, and make blood issue as much as you see; then tighten and bind it, until it is healed; and I have already said incision and cautery in the first book.  
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The blood of the two arteries that are in the two temples, it is good for old migraine and sore eye and accustomed ophthalmia, and to the body of tears of the eyes; and the qualities of the bleeding, it is as I say: and it is that the patient strains his neck until the two veins appear clearly; and feels the pulse below your right hand, then signs on the inside; then lifts the heart over the vein high in your right index finger, and puts the lancet below, and raises the vein high, and the cut, as you have done in the other two veins, and make correction of blood according to your need; then untie the patient, and put your right hand on the vein for one hour, then put cotton on top; and then tie them together, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken about their cutting and their extraction, or the beginning of the book. 
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bloodletting of the vein of the forehead is worth as much as the bloodletting of the cephalic for old facial diseases, and for migraine, and for a redness; and its qualities are that the patient strains his neck by twisting it, until the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "digger," whose shape is here: 
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point on the vein, and firm support with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see; then tie around the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is healed and never work it with a wide flame. 
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it does not suit that the flames are too thick; and the healing across, because the bone is near, and by chance breaks the flame when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood of the two veins that are in the two tear ducts helps the eyes, and the nose, and the cheek, and the corner of the eye, and diseases of the face; and the qualities of their blood is that the patient straitens his neck by twisting with any linen, as before; then the vein, and be the vein through, a bit through the length of the flame a bit wide, because there is no flesh.  
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, by chance it breaks; then make a correction of the blood, as much as you need, and then tie up cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bloodletting of the vein near the nose is good for ague, and for feverish sickness, and for diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, even when it is old; and the qualities of the blood are that the patient tightens his collar, then strains his neck to your left hand, and takes a subtle long flame, and puts it between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well there, and the vein will now begin to flow; and do not allow too much to be taken out, and make bloodletting according to your necessity, then bind it for a night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame: 
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bloodletting of the II veins helps in the treatment of the ailments, and at the beginning of the disease, and a multitude of diseases, and at epilepsy, and at corrosions, and at herpes, and scabies; and the qualities of the bloodletting are that the patient should restrain his neck from one side to the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing above the head of the patient, and the patient sitting on the seat, then bleed the vein of the long one a little widely, then draw out blood moderately, or as much as is necessary; then redo another part in the other vein, then untie the tie, and restrain all the veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle; and leave him until morning, that the wound may be healed. 
de la sainie des leivres	of the vein of the books 
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the upper lips helps in collection in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and fissures of lips, and sores and inflammation.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the vein are that you make the patient sit in front of you, and restrain his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one is to the right lip and the other to the left, and know them by those that are black, and by those that around them have small black veins: therefore cut both, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, so cut the largest of each side, and also do of the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner. 
de la sainie desoz la lengue	from the vein below the tongue 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bloodletting of the veins that are below the tongue so helps after the bleeding of the cephalic, and it is to the treatment of the throat, and the diseases of the eye, and the diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of the bloodletting are that the patient lies between your hands in front of the sun, and he lifts the tongue, and looks below on each side a black vein: bleed therefore one and the other, and do not go too deep into them, because below there are the arteries.  
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins by the cut of which one commonly bleeds are bled in two ways: either they prick at their entire flame mirror wide, or olive subtle as a cutter trenchant, and is called "anesil"; and are wide and subtle according to the width and the strictness of the veins. 
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame mirror is very well-known, and is as wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And there is need to open the veins with a flat and large blood containing vessels, and that contain much blood and thick; and this is the form of the olive flame. 
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And is more subtle pointed, and is for healing veins subtly, where there is subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are under the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly; and it befits the surgeon to cut sagely, and to avoid the artery that is below.  
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it cuts the earth, and a flow of blood comes, then you should cauterize it as I said; and it must not be pricking flame, but cutting like an axe. 
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, then it is necessary that you restrain it and change another; or you want any vein of it, or you heal in its place the vein with the arm: it opens manifestly; and the cup to the flame anesil, as we have said. 
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see to know the place of the vein, then it is necessary that you extract the arm, that you touch the place as long as you know the pulse; then sign the place with ink, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein of the flame vessel; and ward that you do not wound in the artery when you see the place inflamed, for it is from the artery: avoid therefore.  
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it bulge upwards like the urine of a child, and the skin is red and smooth, know that it is blood from an artery: hurry then, and put your hand lengthwise on it, then remove your hand if the wound is bleeding; if he cries out, and let him lie still, and do not move him; be afraid, and do not move him until it is healed.  
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound is not stretched and it aches, and the medicine is not present, then close the artery if it opens, because the head of the retraction; and stretch the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a strip of fig, and make it into strips, and take one of the halves and bind it well until the other day; if it does not hurt, that is good; if not, cure it, as we have said, with powders that stop blood; and the stopping does not sting in many positions for the small place of the wound, and the feeling of the linen of the arm. 
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The blood of the vein in the middle so aids that it draws blood from above the head and from below the body because it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic, as we have said; and it behooves the surgeon that he place himself for the nerve which is below, and if it is not too deeply drawn out, and he finds the nerve, and he swells and the patient feels pain, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some men because of its subtlety, then it behooves that you feel it from the instrument anesil; and withdraw the nerve to your power. 
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if it has a vein between the two nerves, then make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The vein of the head helps so that it draws blood from the head and helps the eyes; and it is necessary to bleed by pricking it in the olive branch or in the myrtle branch because it is the safest of all veins because it does not have nerves or arteries underneath. 
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest position, and do not grieve if one must try for the first time, and start again; and by chance it swells the joints in some men, when one tries for the first time, but it does not cause harm. 
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing that you must know of bloodletting, if it is brought to bear only for keeping health, and for avoiding the diseases to come; and let the bloodletting be done in one of the III veins that are or: that is to say, cephalic, femoral, and basilica; and one must bloodletting at the beginning of Lent on foot, and in autumn and in winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and one must bloodletting the first day or the third, after II hours or III dou days. 
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bloodletting which is administered to the sick does not have a certain hour, but when it is necessary by day or by night, at all hours and in all times; and it is not good to bleed children until XIV years, nor women carrying fruit from the fourth month until the seventh.  
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Do not bleed those who are over sixty years old.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when some one wants to be bled, in what manner that it may be, it is necessary that he should make empty the intestines with a light enema, if he has much of phlegm retained, so that the veins do not attract the superfluities rotten harmful to the principal members; and let no one be bled who is too full of flesh, nor who is drunk, as long as he is thus, nor those who are dropsy; and it is worse to bleed after colic passion, and vomiting, and loosening of belly, and multiplication of labor in woman, and travel, and watching and fasting, and anything that weakens the virtue, or by thing of the arm or of the body; then purify the humors, if he has a lot, by flesh and by drinks and by medicines, if you have the power; then enter into a bath, if nothing prevents you, to purify the blood, and bleed from the vein of the wrist, as we have said; and keep yourself that day from work, and from pain, and from lust, and similar things; and be lie down and joyful, and let the one who is bled be higher than he who bleeds him, and rub his arm two or three times, then restrain the ligature above the middle, because when it is too tight or loose, it cannot correct the blood; and then rub the place with your hands, until the veins swell, and you feel them; then moisten the one who is bled with a little bit of old oil, then put his finger of his left hand on that vein under the place where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not be and fail when it is pierced. 
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that are as thick as cords in the body, and some are so full of windiness, that when one puts the flame on them, they retract from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus it is with some; and if he opens the vein, then the wound is too tight, for this reason the practitioners should be advised about these things. 
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good; if not, he begins again a little below where it was or above, if the place is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the swelling is inflamed, and the patient fears, let him leave it for one or two days, and not bind the arm: by chance there will come boils; do not enter into a bath, then restart the bloodletting if he pleases; and if the wound is small, or the vein short subtly and you doubt that there isn't as much blood as you see, so fire in that same wound all the flame directly; and make it pierce gently, thus that the swelling be inflamed; for this happens many times, when the wound is small. 
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place inflamed, do not begin the bleeding again, and put a little bit of oil there, because it calms the body of blood, and is more suitable in this place than the lie that the oil; and thus administer the ointment of oil in each cut that you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and the same thing does triacle and balm of them, when one puts it on the place; so subtly the bleeding and separates when it is too large. 
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which happens often, even when it is not drained except for the time when the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and put on the place a sponge moistened in water and a little hot, and hold it for an hour; and it is necessary that you do this after the blood flow from the vein, and if it remains in its place after several days without any blackness or greenness, it does not harm him; and if you see it, put on top of anything aloes or myrrh remixed with juice of calamine, monument, or similar. 
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscesses and appearances at the wound of the basilica happen: put therefore your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft to the compression of the hand, so is that appearance bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore avoid that you put on anything of those things we have said, for by chance it cuts without the artery; but make  one plaster dry to harden the place, then cure it with another cure, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each according to the quantity of his virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it bleed until it is red; and if you see it swollen, let it subside until it becomes thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for him who is plump and strong, and has need of bloodletting, to make a wider wound, and let the flames be wide; and for him who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed him little by little and often, and one must bleed him by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of bleeding is safe from a decrease of blood and a severing of nerve, and is worth more than the bleeding done through the long or the wide. 
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to him whose body needs bloodletting, it is necessary to give soft bread in pomegranate juice; if he is hot, treat with blood III times or IV And if he is of cold complexion, let him take beforehand soft bread in mule syrup, or in honey aromatic syrup with spices, like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup. 
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it bleeds at the vein, after the outflow of much blood, it is necessary that he moisten a broth of flesh and fragrant syrup and uses other things that we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of the vein. 
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to bleed his arm, and bleed another time, if it is necessary, when he is weakened by much bleeding, that he bleeds little by little, according to the quantity of his virtue continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to bleed his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, then he bleeds seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to bleed from another place, then he must bleed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body that has already coagulated, and it brings fever; so it is necessary to draw a great quantity, and widen the opening until it flows in small pieces; then when you have fulfilled all the conditions of health, and put your hand upon his arm while he heals, that death may not come in place of the wound, and this happens many times, when the healer is negligent; and it is not fitting when you see untie the arm, and make blood flow a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press strongly; nor if it is curved, that you extend the arm greatly, because this would be bad; but let it remain until he heals the second time; or you point to the tip of the flame, as long as the blood which is frozen at the opening of the vein flows out, and put upon I spot of wool placed in water, and press lightly. 
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and do not tighten it at all, until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires bleeding a second time, let it be done in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is bled in place of the vein in the neck because it is composed
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of this vein is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the bone is red; then it is bound moderately so that the vein appears well, then the leech is now drawn through, neither too wide nor too long; and let the punctures be wide, and let the leeching be done close to the joint of the hand, and if he cannot draw any out, put his hand back in hot water, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; and if it is in summer, do not put his hand back in hot water, because it is put there more in winter than in summer; and the leeching of this vein is safer of all other veins, because there is neither artery nor nerve. 
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The blood of the salvation of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: strain the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein is swollen, if one sees it; and if the vein is sideways, and if you cut it entirely, it does not grieve anything; and do not let it be too much profaned, for the nerves are under all naked flesh, and then put the hand back into hot water, if the blood is congealed in the wound, and cannot issue. 
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary, then put oil and wool on the vein to stop it firmly, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The vein of them in the left hand is equal to the disease of the mouse, and do all as I have told you towards right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sap of the sophene is good for all illnesses that are below the body, such as illnesses of the marrow, and retention of flowers, and illness of the reins, and hips and legs and similar illnesses. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its salve are that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it is sore, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many veins; so moisten where more broad vein or at the ankle, which he deems best. 
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you bleed it on the foot, ward off the nerves that are below, and make the cut across as when cutting; and let the flame be untied.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot feel it, put the foot in water, and leave the vein to bleed well open.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the vein must be cut the first time, then it begins again above a point, because the place is salty; do not doubt of the nerve, as we have said, and thus make from the spine of the other leg equally.  
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle, and its incision relieves pain in the hip, when it is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the qualities of his vein are that the patient enters into bath and is strained above the ankle four times by twisting, for otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, so you put on the sail in all ways that you can, and by crossing; and it is better that you cut it, because the skin is dry, and she is well recovered by hand.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, so healthy any vein of him who opens or back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and guard the nerves; and make as much correction of blood that you see, and then untie the bandage, and put on cotton and restrain it; she is now healed. 
des sainies de ventouse	of the leeching of a suction cup 
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction cups are made of horns, or glass, or wood; and suction is done in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is done with fire is according to II manners: or it is with all fire, or without fire; and cupping which is done by wounding and extracting blood is done in XIV places of the body, of which one is whole in the head; and the other is in the neck; and II others in II ribs of the neck; and the cup on below the chin; and the cup on the II shoulders; and the cup above the hips; and the cups between the II arms; and the cups on the II legs; and the cups on the II ankles; and cupping does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and because of this it does not weaken at all, as one does with blood from a vein; and it should not be administered, either with all fire or without fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied. 
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of diseases it is necessary to bloodletting, or for customs, we shall administer each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in every time; because there are such that when they have need for bleeding, they have a heavy head; and there are who feel repletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness around their eyes; and some who feel a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and spit blood; and there are those who dream, and see by blood and numbness and death and similar things.  
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and even when it is in the middle of the month, we command them to vomit after 3 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bloodletting of the temple helps to treat the headache... that comes to the eyes, and it is not fitting that this be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventilation is in place of the bloodletting of the head, and it is not fitting that those who are of a cold complexion use it, or who have cataracts, because it does much harm to them; and for this reason it is not fitting that the elderly use it, nor those who have or cold diseases.  
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become oblivious, and for this reason it is necessary to put the suction cup a little lower down due to the fear of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation of the neck is in the place of the vein of the head and of the basilica, and for this reason it is good for the tightening of the groin, and for opening the channel of the womb, and for all, and for repletion; and one should not put it too tightly, because if it holds too firmly, it engenders a blockage in the stomach or in the heart. 
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, and obtalmie and emigrainne, and a l’estranglement, and a la dolor as racines des dens, and est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; and covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, and ne veigne decorremens de sanc. 
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventilations under the chin are worth for mouth disease, and gum decay, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is good for the illness that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The incisions of the veins are as valuable as three veins of the arm because they draw blood from these large veins; and instruct the patient not to make them too deep, for the skin is bare of flesh and near nerves and arteries. 
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup which is on the rump is good for hemorrhoids from the foundation, and for diseases below, and it is necessary that the suction cup be large, and be of iron, that it has need to well milk; and perchance, if it was subtle, it would break; and I make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups of the legs are applied openly, because they attract blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains of the reins, and of the thighs, and of the bladder, and soften the flowers; and are in their place of two shins, and of two ankles, and nevertheless they weaken the body after long use, and bring weakness in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of putting on the suction cup is that you put it first empty, and succeed temperately, and put it gently, and move evenly, and do not cease from doing this, until you see the place red and inflamed, and appear the color of blood; then firm, and replace the suction cups, and take care in the disposition of the bodies, because there are such who have tender flesh, and clear pores: so it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and a prick deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, it is necessary to prick it twice: the first time to make a subtle passage for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it is necessary to prick it a third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, we only pierce once.
