Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, as long as you are on the fracture; and know which is the fracture and the figure of it; and if the fracture is at the top only, so put equal the fracture, as long as it is to natural figure.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it declines to the inside, so make the patient lie on their belly, as long as the restoration of that fracture be apparent to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have put it even, put it on the plaster, then put on a splint of wood or of horn, and restrain the bandage so that it does not move; and apply the place under the ribs, until the ligament is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on his healthy rib or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes there, do not touch it until the abscess is calmed, and put on what we have said before; and then return to restoration, and restrain it as is proper, if there is no bad accident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the shoulder and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one must restore it according to one of the two ways: one of which is that you take a single stick of medium thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two heads two strings, and bend them upward, and place the patient on one seat; then lay his broken arm on the stick, as far as it reaches to the armpit, and make a curvature of the stick in the middle, then place on any heavy thing or the ministers extend it downward; then put the mirrors the fracture equal to their hands together, until the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one supports the patient on his back, and ties his hand to his neck, then commands two ministers that one holds that which is above the fracture with their hands, and the other holds below at one length, and extend each to their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more out, restrain the ligament under the fracture, and over the fracture, and extend each minister to its side. 
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the shoulder, it is necessary to put one band under the breastbone and the other towards the side, under the fracture; and also if the fracture is towards the side, it is necessary to put the band lightly, without effort, until the fracture is equal on top and on the side; then put the fracture in place as it should, and restrain it, if a boil does not come. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess comes, do not restrain it until seven days, and put on a linen cloth moistened in honey and rose oil, until the abscess calms; then restrain (it), and the manner of restraining it is that you place the splint on the fracture, then assemble the arm on the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the drape, and restrain on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its right place, unless something prevents you, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not moving, use splints, and place on the fracture a splint larger and stronger than the others, and have between each splint two fingers of space, and be each splint so large that it passes over the fracture three fingers on each side; then restrain on the splints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the fracture, more strongly and less in widening.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the seat of the splints and the tightening, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the hot abscess, then let it be bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then look every three days the bond, that itching or swelling does not come to the place, or the numbing does not come to the limb for that he is too foreign.  
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it occurs, as we have said. 
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents come, then do not untie it before III days or more, and have the patient sleep on his back, and have his hands on his stomach; and put under the shoulder one cushion full of wool evenly, and look each hour of the day or of the night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or be softened the ligaments; if the receive by the virtue of medicine, and give him the meat that we have before set out, in such a manner that the meat is at first subtle; and when he begins to recover, let it be coarse. 
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be taken back in forty days from all; and then one must untie and administer baths and ointments to heal the place. 
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is bad and clogged, it remains for a day or two months to be untied. 
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of .ij. bones, which are called the two "fossiles," because one is small, and it follows the pocket; and the other is large, and it is below, toward the small toe; perhaps the large fossil breaks alone, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when the large ones are broken, the healing is bad, and more grieves than when they are broken together. 
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small bone that is broken alone, then it should be gently extended and made even. 
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the great fossa, then it is necessary to pull harder; and extend it above the cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the small toes lower than the other toes, and let the patient be crossed on himself, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then extend the ministers with your arm to the part below his hand, or at the knee, and one other minister to the other above.  
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the mirrors equal, according to its best form. 
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is any detached that grasps the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do as above with the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter; so take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of the restoration abscesses come out, then glue a cloth made of rose oil and white wax, that it be neither too hard nor too soft; and lay the cloth carefully on top, until the abscesses are calmed.  
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then put the plaster on the cerote, and place the molding powder with an abundance of egg there, then put the splints on, and let the splint of the breakage be a little more outward, and a little wider than the others; and know that it must have VI splints or arms in more arrangements: whether the breakage is in one of the bones, or two; and tighten more above the breakage than elsewhere, and every day less as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the coverings that are on the splint be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; and let the thread with which it is strained be of linen, neither too thick nor too fine, as we have said. 
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the ligature after some days. 
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accidents come to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, it is necessary that you raise the limb in hot water, until the itch is appeased; and let the limb not be too much at rest.  
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin the tightening again, and if the ligaments are loosened and the bones dislocated, and similar things, so as to address it. 
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if it happens that the numbing cannot come to the limb, because it is too constricted, then it is necessary that you soften it a little, and leave thus some days, until the numbing comes, and then constrain it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, do not unbind him until 20 days. 
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or when the neck is bent, then he lays his hands on his neck and makes his collarbones even and guards against movement and agitation, and sleeps on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or thirty-five days, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the constitutions and the complexities of virtues. 
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and as we have two it comes but little fractures, and there comes only many times a sprain.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or sprained, it befits the patient to sit crossed, and to be straight before him as well; then put his hand on top stretched, and extend the ministers the broken bones, and set them equal the mire, until they are well joined; and put the plaster and bandages, if abscesses do not come, then he puts a splint according to the quantity of the place; and be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is at the bottom towards the belly of the palm, make a sphere of cloth, and command the patient to tighten it to his broken palm; and then strain with a long cloth, and let the splint be of tough stuff as big as the palm of the hand, and strain it, as it befits.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the forearm, you must put a splint on top and another underneath in the palm, so that the hand be open and straight, then tie it tightly around the hand, and staunch the connection between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of the two [arms], if it is the ulna, put it straight as it should be; and restrain it with the palm, and if you see fit put a small straight splint to raise the fracture, so that it does not move; and if the fracture is in the other bones, as in the index or one of the others, put it straight, and tie it with the healthy bone which comes after; or you tie them all together in one holding, whichever is better, or put a splint on top like a sling; and take heed in the restoration and in the disposition of an abscess hot, and secure what comes to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken hip
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the hip is many times broken, and it can be seen well when it turns forward and backward; and its restoration is done by binding one above the fracture, and one below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then extend each minister his band to his side equally; and this is when the fracture is between the bones.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the hip, one ligament should be towards the sword hilt, and the other ligaments below the fracture. 
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is near the knee, and therefore let the ligaments be below the knee, and let the extension be down; then put your hands on the bone equal to its two hands, until it is according to its natural figure, and then put the splint, and the tie, so that no abscess comes. 
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it appease then return to your work and your care; the tie is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap the fracture with a thick bandaged doubled in II or III, and keep the superfluities, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and put the long thread between the hip and the leg, below the knee, and bring the head of the thread upwards; then turn upwards the leg and on the hip the bandage, then place above the fracture splints, and place a splint on the bone of the leg; then employ the space between the leg and the hip with cloths soft to put equal pressure, then begin to bind firmly III turns or IIII on the fracture; and as much as you go higher up from the fracture, and less restrain it; then take hold of the II heads of the thread that you have put between the leg and the hip, and tie III splints that are above, then return downwards to the head of the thread, until you come near the foot; and restrain it, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, then let it not come an abscess or swelling nor any other appearance. 
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, untie it, and address what comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that pierce, it is necessary to remove them, if one can; and if one cannot, it is necessary to split the place, and draw out the pus; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the hip is broken as one puts splints in it, like in the shoulder and the arm; however, in this restoration done does not ring the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the hip is restored in one day, or a little less or a little more, according to the diversity of temperaments.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the  knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the joint of the knee there are few fractures, but it bends many times. 
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is no longer just a fissure, or a puncture wound, and it becomes any kind of wound, and without a wound, and everyone feels it well. 
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is done by putting each thing that is round in its place, as long as it can be assembled and moved; then put the splint on it, and put a rounded stele on it, if you need it, and restrain it as necessary, then return to all the arrangements that we have said in other fractures, such as hot poultices and similar things; so put on each accident what it needs, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, so one is called by right "tibia," and the other is called "fibula"; and it has all the same fracture as it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is like that of the arm equally, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns in every way. 
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and one sees it well; and it turns downwards.  
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore administer extension, and set it equal, and tie the limbs equally; but nonetheless, if the fracture is bad, and there are many pieces, that the extension be less and lighter; and the splint according to your virtue. 
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two bands of splints that encompass the leg on both sides, and be as long as the leg from the knee down; then wrap in two layers one bandage above and below, and tie it in the middle, also, and at this juncture the leg will not be able to decline to right or left, and thus is well. And none administers a single splint along the length of the leg, and if it is of wood, and it is placed on the leg to ward off movement, and properly one does this in the fracture where there is a wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or other accident; so cure until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	To the ankle does not come any fracture, but to the bones of the foot comes no time fracture and two parts, and there happen only as much in more positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there happen the bones of the foot fracture, and you see these bones overlapping each other, put the patient's foot on the ground, as if he would like to walk, and then put your foot on his, where the bones are raised, then press them until they return to their places; then put the splint and bandages on it, and put under the belly of the foot a small board at 2 fingers wide, then restrain the foot firmly, and after that you have wrapped cloths around it, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when 3 days or 4 will have passed, you untie the linen, because you will find the bones aligned, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the bones broken, restore them as we have said about the bones of the hand; then put on the broken bone a splint according to the length of the bone, and be one poke more wide, then put under the foot that table that I have said, and restrain well. And if there are .ij. or .iij., or more, broken, put on each bone a splint according to its quantity, wrapped in one cloth of linen, and restrain the table under the foot; and let it be standing on the top of the table outside the belly of the foot, so that it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about the other fractures, as we have said; and cure each accident as it is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the woman's nature is broken, make her sit down enlarged, then incline it to the back part, and hold it in the back; then fill the basin of the woman with cotton, and put as much in as the fist; then take out the woman, and lift her back up and down, and then jump the cotton, until it comes to the entrance of nature, and the bone returns with the fist; and when she wants to pee, take out the cotton, and when she has peed, put it back, and do this for VII days or about that: so the fracture will be restored, and if you see, take a bladder of sheep, and tie it at the opening a chain, and put the whole bladder in nature; then blow into the chain, forming, until the bladder is inflated inside: nature will return the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it like that for some days, until it is healed. 
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the finger of the man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said in the bone of the hip; and are not concealed these fractures near to him who puts his study and his use there, and attend my book.  
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture signifies to many the right way of restoration therefore.  
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the phallus, when it is broken, take a goose's throat and put it into the phallus; then wrap cloths around it, and leave it for .iij. days or around, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bones of the hip or shoulder or similar, that they be treated now, so that the treatments that we have said testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is clean, then retain the vitriol, if you have nothing else, and then begin to restore the fracture in the same hour, or on that day, if there does not come an abscess.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess does come, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, as long as the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it neither on the third nor fourth day, for you would bring a bad accident upon it.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is appearing on the uncovered chest, then it befits that you put it gently in place with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension does not suit you to put it straight with your hands, then resort to this instrument which is of iron, which is .vij. or .viij. long, and its width is according to the quantity of the wound; and for this, it is necessary that the maker imprints .iii. or iiij., according to what he needs in each cure of a fracture; and be round and about an inch thick, so that it does not bend under compression on the member during your work, and be tapered at the front, and thicker from the middle forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And is called "palainche", for which the shoulder bone must be placed on top of the visible bone; and it should be pushed at once, until it returns, and be equal to each other. 
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, then it is necessary that you cut the head of the bone, until the instruments have hold. 
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, then cut it with a suitable instrument, either an incisor or a saw, to your power; then clean that which is left in the bone of asperities and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is brought back, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place. 
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do so until it is in its place, then moisten the drape with black stichtic wine, and properly cover it if there is an injury; and do not put any above the wound, such as cerote or anything else where there is oil, lest it cause rot and corruption; then administer splints when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and warn carefully that the wound is not strained with the fracture; and many times have fools done this, and brought upon the patient either death or corrosion at any time; and let the strapping be softer and more gentle than other fractures.  
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident may happen, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then it is not necessary to put on bandages; but wrap around, in place of bandages, hard cloths, and tie them. 
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two an in-growth on the wound, remove those that you have placed over all wine and place healing ointment for wounds, such as ointment tetraformation and similar.  
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you unbind the member two times a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is fused and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the member be pulled apart in such a manner that the bone goes down easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if each day it passes, and it cannot fuse but returns to its place again, know that there are small fragments of bone, which is why it is necessary that you cover the wound with a cloth, and remove all these loose fragments which cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or other manner of corruption, then it is necessary that you cure it, according to what he says in his chapter previously. 
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, like the bones of the hip or shoulder, and other similar large limbs, do not treat it, because many times death comes from it, but leave it until it rots; perhaps after twenty days or thirty it will heal itself, then cure the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, leave it. 
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Of burns which come from the burn
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the health of the fracture, even when it's near the joint, and a bad thing is to see the figure of the limb; and by chance it cannot make the limbs its natural works.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take ward therefore if it is fresh: If you administer medicines astringents, such as aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, in the way that you take any of these things, or all together, and mix them with astringent wine or with beaten egg white or with oil; and put it on the wound in poultices, and bind it well, and do not loosen it in hands for days; and then untie it, and begin another one, as long as the swelling is removed; or you bind upon a piece of plank well made; because the properties of wood are that it removes all the swellings from the limbs; and if the swelling has already been converted into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut above it, and make the superfluity apparent; or you reapply it to any razor, as long as it is removed, and the cure as long as it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb that is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is restored, and afterwards the limb remains weak and subtle, this happens for many reasons: one reason is because it was bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should; or because there were too many bindings, and it could not come to nursing the member; or for multitude of dressings; or for too great movements, not at its time; or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body supple, until the blood is multiplied in him; and administer bath, and give him joy and lightness; then put poultices on the limb, so that the poultice attracts great nursing, and the dressing often of warm water, until the nursing cures to the member; and returns to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the limb twisted after the healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bones are apart, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nonetheless it does not lose its natural function: so do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb anew, and many foolish people have done this in our land; and this work is blamed, and comes great harm, and by chance death; nonetheless, if the nodes and the torments are fresh, then it behoves them to be raised with hot water, or softening herbs are cooked, such as leaves of marsh mallow, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and the make i. a softening plaster, such as diaconium well made, and you take the mash of marsh mallow, and you confit it with fat of geline or oil of sesame, and make a plaster on top; or you take figs fatty, and grind them with hemp of colon, and similar medicines that lessen the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes is dislocation removed by rubbing continuously and lengthily with wet hands. 
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be movement to the limb every hour.  
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the torsion is ingrained and hardened, as well as stone, and there is need to remove it with iron, then it behooves to cut up to the bone, with a subtle, light incision; and put care and study into the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation is from any joint out of its place, for which it cannot move, and the limb is misaligned, and the patient feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, now it is necessary to bring back without strapping.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, then the member swells, and perhaps if one tries to put it back in place, it causes pain; for this reason it is not fitting to move it when it is swollen: many times it brings on lameness and other pains; however, when this happens, first make the patient bleed, then leave them alone, until the abscesses are calmed; then apply hot water and oil, then reset it gently, and cure each member as you would bring it back into place. 
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of dislocations of the head to the foot.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Sometimes it happens that the jaws are dislocated backwards, and the dislocations of both are according to 2 manners: or they are a little bit removed from their places, and softened a little; or they are dislocated entirely, and hang towards the cheek, and cut off the saliva from the mouth so that he cannot hold it, nor can close his mouth, and encircles his tongue with the word.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by the more dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, then you must reset it carefully, and do not delay; and in such a manner that the minister holds the head of the patient, and puts his fingers into the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other two hands should be outside, to put it even; and command the patient to soften them, his jaws, and move them in all directions. 
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the fist he puts even, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is brought back injured, even if they are the two jaws together, apply hot water and oil to them, as long as you gently move them; do not fear to bring it back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the patient is well closed without softening, put on cloths moistened in cerote made of rose oil and wax, then tie it lightly with soft bandages; and let the patient sleep on his back, and his shoulders be between two cushions, so that he does not move them neither to the right nor to the left, nor does he strive to chew, but takes light food, as long as the pains are removed, and the jaws are healed; and then eat what he wants lightly, and does not try to open his mouth to eat and drink, until the jaw is well set and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be put back in place within an hour, and are not converted to their places, then fever and accustomed sores come, and perhaps a bellyache, and perhaps pure vomit.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a peril; and many times die those who have it, within 8 days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The splinter cannot dislocate from the rib inside the continuity of it and of the hip, and is dislocated no time at the outside, and well it is felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies soundly on his back, and stretches his arms; then press the place firmly with your palm, and it will return; then put on the splint and bandage, and restrain it; and the head which is towards the outside cannot dislocate; if perhaps, and if it dislocates any time, you reset it to its place, as we have said; then put on the splint and bandage, and restrain it, and command the patient that he rest until he be healed; and in the same way is brought back the head of the shoulder, when it is dislocated from its place. 
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in only three ways: one is that it is dislocated to the part of the seat toward down; and the second is to the part of the breast; and by chance dislocated to the upper part, and this happens little; and does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and does not dislocate inside for the nerves; and many times dislocated down towards the seat, especially those who have little flesh, because at these it goes easily; at those who have enough flesh, it goes with pain, and enters with pain. 
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And perhaps it happens to some men a percussion or fracture, and inflames the shoulder with a hot abscess, and thinks that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore you must feel it, as long as you are certain; and then commence the cure.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And is known the dislocations when it is drawn toward the seat, and puts difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between their diversity manifest; and you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow, and below the seat to touch the head of the shoulder, as if it were ones; and the patient cannot bring back his hand to its place, nor move from any movements; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, because you find it manifestly at the touch; and this manner of dislocation is not much for bringing back, when it is new, or if the child is sick. 
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the ministers lift the hand of the sick person upward, then put their shoulders under the seat, and lift the joint with force upward to its place; and the ministers lift the hand, and extend it upward, then put it down; so it will come gently.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in a few days after, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and administer softening and soothing ointment, such as decoction of althea and fenugreek and melilot in water, and let it be administered; then lay the patient on his back, and put under his seat a pad of wool equal, neither too soft nor too hard, then put the heel of the foot on the pad, and lift the head of the shoulder carefully, and pull the hand of the patient; and another minister holds the head of the patient so that it does not move down; this shoulder returns now, and if you see that you reset it according to this manner: and it is that you make present a man who is larger than the patient; and be right towards the side, and put his shoulder under the seat of the patient, and lift the seat up, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister pulls the hand of the patient down towards the belly. 
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, so it can with him no heavy thing, and the dislocation returns now. 
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And reset it in another way: and is one stick long in the earth, whose head is as if the post, and not too thick nor too thin; then it is placed below the patient, but that he has blankets above, and the patient lies on the long end of the shaft; then his hand is extended to the other side forming, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all these things we have said, so do this cure: take a stick of two arms of great and four fingers of wide, which has the head round for to enter in the shaft below the armpit, according to this form: 
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie above the head of the staff cloths soft, that the staff does not bruise the patient, then put it under the shoulder of the patient; and extend his arm on the length of the staff, and tie the shoulder onto the staff, and the arm to the head of the hand, then put the arm on one rung of a ladder wide, and let the hands be stretched down, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is ens, in whatever manner that it may be, so it behoves you to put under the saddle a sphere of wool even, then put the plaster covered with powder of the mill, with incense and auburn of egg, over all the shoulder and around, then strain it under the saddle evenly, and turn the linen upon the plaster, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it behoves that he massage little, as long as the limb is fortified, because it will heal more quickly; and then massage later after 5 days or 7, and move it; and if it is hardened and is not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place because of moisture that has come or for another cause, then it befits you to administer cautery at three points, as it is shown in the chapter on cautery. 
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all these things, and it loosens after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift his arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is toward the hip, and the breasts, or rear, is made by impulse, and stretching of hands, and it is administered in another place; and treatment until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes pain to the limb, and slow movements, then the patient uses baths many times, until that pain is alleviated, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the hinge
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the hinge joint is dislocated to points, and to points it returns; and if it has been dislocated from all sides, and even in front and behind, and the dislocation is not set because it can be seen well and felt well; and dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the blade of the cautery with the healthy one, if you can see it clearly. 
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all. 
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it in the same way as an abscess should come to a head, because if an abscess should come to a head, it would be harmful to bring it back; and perhaps it cannot be brought back completely at all, even when it is in the rear; so it is worse than other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and perhaps death comes from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is thus, when it is such that one can bring it back, that you extend your hand to its two hands; and his arms be spread, and the hands do move according to the cut around, above and below, and put the joint to its shoulders together, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when it doubles its hand to its hand, and firm of the root of the palm the cut which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and that two ministers extend the arm, and hold them with two ministers, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm on each side, then when you have enveloped a double long and wide cloth; and when the minister joins the joint with his hand, he puts oil of any kind to soften the joint, then pushes the joint together, until it returns; and when it is in place, put a dry plaster above with a yolk of egg, and hold it firmly, and bend the arm to the neck of the sick person, and leave it for some days, then untie it. 
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the bandage, and let it be; and if you see that the joint does not tighten well, start the plaster and bandage again, and let it so for some days, until it is firmly set; then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the return of the joint, and it moves, bathe him well and rub him, and press until he is appeased; or you put on the joint a sheepskin fat, then let it rest one day and night, then take the bone, and let it enter the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint moderately, then put the sheepskin back, and then enter the bath; and thus do it two or three times, until it is cured; and if you see, put on a fleece of moistened wool heated with butter, and strain it over; it will return to its place.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its return is light, more than other joints Nevertheless, it is necessary to bring it back to its place immediately, as soon as it is dislocated, so that the limb does not become swollen or that an abscess comes up hot.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the putting back is that you place the diseased hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and he makes it even, so that it puts its palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes it until it comes back whole; it behooves you to see if it is well in place; then put the patient's back of his hand on a table for extension and putting back. 
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, the patient puts their back of their hand on the table, and the surgeon places their hand on the appearance of the joint.  
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is good. 
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after some days, then the joint remains twisted; and harms nothing to the patient further than while the hand is weak, and cannot restrain anything at all: therefore know that the nerves are cut, or the artery; so there is no other means except to restrain by cautery according to the case, and perhaps there is no other thing.  
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the splint that we have said, then constrain and leave it for five days, then unbind and let it be so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is no injury, then moisten with hot water, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocation of the wrists of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the thumbs are dislocated on each side, sometimes on the back of the palm or on the belly; therefore, is the thumb and puts the dislocation in your pouches until it returns, then support the head of the thumb and the bend towards the part where it is disjoined; and let it II days, and then put it even that day; and do not tie it, as we have said, and untie it from day to day, and make it move, and tie it again; and do this often, until it is tight, and just as well, if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you did before, until it is healed; and just as well, when it is dislocated on another part. 
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the shoulder blade
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade of the back or neck is dislocated, or there are more dislocations, if there is no cure, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs of this are that the gestions jump out without willing, and cannot hold it, and many times are softened any member, or the two hips or the two arms or one. And many times the leg moves at four parts; the one who moves to the rear is called «gilbositez»: the cure of this is that you reward oneself if the gilbositez has come from childhood: if there is not a cure nor healing of all. 
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And those that come from a fall or percussion or similar things, the ancients said ways of cures with great words, where there is not in all much benefit; but I have abridged it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in diverse ways.  
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the swelling that comes to the breast before, there is nothing that heals; and also that which comes straight in II sides, and one cannot cure except properly that which comes to the back, as I say; and it is that the patient be stretched upon his face in I place equal, and have strain under him, so that he does not tremble; then put the stick at the head in earth forming, and the other at the feet, and tie a linen band between the shoulders of the patient, and the other at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two ministers hold the bands, one at the head and the others at the feet, among the II sticks; and be well closed, the stick as we have said, and the mire puts his palms upon the spine forming, until it returns. 
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, then take a board three arms long, and lay it under the armpit, and have the patient lie on his side, and put the head of the board under the armpit, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and put the feet of the patient on the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see that, do the same to the opposite one which turns by hand.  
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.
