And it is that you put II twigs at the head of the sick man's arm of a great, and towards the feet II others, and there are between each twig, under and above, a palm's width of long; and have in each twig I pierced, where the string runs, and be the twigs firmly in the earth so that they do not move; and between II twigs there is one turning twig, on which the cord turns, and have in II turning II small twigs of a palm’s length, to turn the twine; and then tie the cord which is among the splints to the string towards the head, and the other cord towards the feet to the other string, and each of the ministers turns his string to all the cord, and the master puts the spine straight as we have said. 
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is leveled, put a drying plaster with an abundance of egg, and then the bandages, and then the splint of a tablet of III digits long, that reaches the place of the gibbosity and the part of the spine healthy, then tie it with a band, as we have said, and use the patient of subtle nourishment, until it is healed; and if any thing comes in the end of the healing, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the splint that we have said before; and sometimes one administers a piece of plank, and sometimes it appears in the back spine of the back, and they think that it is dislocations; and it is the bone which opens, for which one must not have presumption: by chance would come death.  
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder come out only as dislocations, and not like other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to .iiij. parts: inside and outside, and front and rear; and more inside then, and little dislocated front and rear.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation inside is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and opens more the patient's knee than the healthy one, and the patient cannot double his knee at all; and it is the leg which is beside inflamed from hot abscess, because the head of the hip comes there.  
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes at the fever, thus is this accident contrary to these before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him to whom it comes at the front, thus is that he is well his leg according to the fulfillment; however, do not double the knee without pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot before, and holds back his urine, and inflames the groin, and when he goes, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him to whom it comes behind, thus is that he cannot spread his knee, nor double, and is that leg more twisted than the other, and the groin is softened, and is the hip bone in place under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The return of this semblance of dislocation is that you watch if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its disposition, then there is no cure; and it does not behoove him to have presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those whose dislocation is fresh, and there are .iiij. manners of dislocation, so haste that you return the joint, and stretch it inside and outside, and move it to the right and left; perchance it will return, and there is no need for other care.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then it behooves you to appear the minister strong, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or at the ligament that is bound above the knee; and another minister extends his hand above in such a manner that he puts his hands below his shoulders, then he squeezes with a firm grip on the hip; and another holds the head of the limb; and extend both upward and downward all at once, until the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains suspended. 
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four likenesses, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If this is not the case, then it is necessary to take care of its semblance. When the dislocation is at the end, then you must support the patient on his healthy side, then put the linen above the root of the hip, and the place that is below the groin, then stretching the linen upwards towards the groin, and towards the force; then seize with other ministers his arms, and embrace the large part of the diseased hip, and extend it outward: now it will return to its place; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than others. 
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tighten it in this manner that we have said, then it behooves you to bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong linen cloth over the two heels, and over the two knees, and let the sick leg be extended two palms more than the other; then let it be hung from the top of a pole, and be above the ground two arms long; then command the minister that he embrace the head of the hip, and let other ministers be hanging with the patient, who embrace firmly the hip, for the joint now returns easily. 
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is at the rear, the patient lies down, as we have said in the one who has gilbosite, and restrain the limb above the bad leg properly, and above the hip too; then put two sticks, one at the top and the other at the feet, then put a stick between the hips of the patient in the middle of the form; and have a plant of moist cloths around it so that it does not bleed the bad leg, then extend each minister towards him, and the mire puts equally in his hand the dislocation. 
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good. 
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If this is not the case, place it on a table, and press it as we have said in the chapter on dislocations, and lay the patient on his healthy side. 
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the diseased leg as far as possible, and according to what I have said; and put the minister's pain on the affected ankle, then press with the other hand, and the extension downward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the hip, it does not behoove to stretch the patient down or raise up on the ground, but it behoove that he be as if the thigh was dislocated at the hip, as we have said about lying on the two hips; and be upon his face, and the bandage stretched as we have said before, and one must press upon the joint to the table; and will be in place when the patient stretches his legs, and they are even; then adjust the thighs, and put the splint, and the strapping of a band, so that the hip does not move; and rest III days or IV, then untie it, and put the splint on; and if you see that they are even, strap it as before, and let it be for III days; then untie it, and let him walk well, until the limb is strengthened. 
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: namely, inside and outside, and behind; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg to his hip, and if it does not rest on his hip, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his thigh, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and retract between your two fingers, then bend the two bones forming the knee; and other ministers extend his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it rests gently on his hip; and put the plaster on top, and make the leg rest on the hip, and tie them together firmly for three days or four, then untie them; and do not let the patient work to go, as long as the limb is strengthened. 
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not set, administer a strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is sound 
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes dislocated and sometimes fully dislocated, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs of this are that the ankle is swollen, and feels ahead to the part where it is dislocated: the resetting is light, and one should extend it gently with one's hands when it is only bruised. 
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated completely, then you must make the patient sit upright, and hold him with your ministers except by the leg, above the ankle; then draw the foot to yourself with your right hand, and then with the left two times, then up the side, and push the foot well upwards; and do this two times, as we have said, pushing and drawing the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, start the operation again, because it will return; and if it cannot return like this, then make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and place a stake firmly in the ground between his thighs, and tie belts around him, so that he does not move; then hold the ministers the thigh, and other ministers extend the foot to their hands or at the groin, so that it lies above the joint of the foot; then extend each minister evenly, and let the stakes be well placed between the patient's thighs in order to retain the patient when being extended; then place the midwives on each side the dislocation with their hands, and other ministers hold the sound leg below, and the dislocation will return easily. 
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is pointed, put the plaster and dressings on top, and strain them, and tie the foot to the leg, and guard the nerves which are above the ankle behind, that the ligatures not be too tight; then let him leave it II days or III, and if the ligatures soften, tighten them again; then untie it at the third day or fourth, and forbid the patient to walk for IIII days; and if he goes before that term, it is not certainty that he does not dislocate again. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to him, then it is necessary that you soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the hips are dislocated, it is well to extend them gently, and this is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the back or foot, then it is necessary that you make the patient sit on a level surface or on a table straight, and put your foot on what separates the joints, then press with your foot firmly, until it returns; and when it is equal and there is nothing apart, then put under the sole of the foot a board at the shoulder, then strain it firmly, and let it for three days, then untie it; and let him rest, as long as he is healed.  
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times happens that the patient dies: so do not be presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and patient, nor rash; and use at the beginning soothing things of hot poultice, and let the patient in God's hand, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, so reset the limb to its place, so that the poultices may come there alive; and when the limb is in place, administer soothing things of hot poultice, and cure the wound as it is right, with drying dressings; and if with the dislocation a fracture, and small bones are separated, set them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and guard yourself from entering into the way of fear, according to what I have said, for this costs you death according to your Creator, and for the safety of your arm and body. 
Amen	Amen
